The Reality and Description of Hell
Commentator explains verse on Hell's reality, layers, and obligation of belief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Hell is a literal, created reality with seven layers, and that belief in it is obligatory based on the Book, Sunnah, and consensus.

Core Idea
Hell is real, created, and its horrors are detailed as a deterrent.

This lesson establishes the reality of Hell as a created abode of punishment. The commentator explains the verse from the poem, affirming Hell's existence and describing its seven layers, its immense heat, and its unique fuel. This knowledge serves as a powerful deterrent for believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the commentator's own rhythm come through before interpreting.
2
Identify the key claims
Notice that the passage asserts Hell is true, created, and belief in it is obligatory. Find the scriptural basis mentioned.
3
Examine the seven layers
The passage lists the seven layers of Hell in order. Observe their arrangement and the detail about their doors.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why such vivid details are given: to instill awe and serve as a deterrent. The final anecdote about worldly fire reinforces this.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بالجنة والنار وخلودهما حسبما علم تفصيلا أو إجمالاً، مع نفي الاحتياج إليها أو العبثية (عَلَيْكَ الإنْسَانُ) المكلَّف، غايته أنَّ الإيمان بها تعبدي .
١٠٩. وَالنَّارُ حقٌّ أُوجِدَتْ كَالْجَنَّةِ فَلَا تَمِلْ لِجَاحِدٍ ذِي جِنَّةِ
(وَالنَّارُ حَقٌّ) أي ثَابتةٌ بالكتاب والسُّنَّة واتفاق عُلماء الأُمَّة ، وكلُّ ما هو كذلك .. فالإيمان به واجب ، إلى هذا ذهبَ جمهورُ أهل السُّنَّة (١) والمُراد مِن النَّار: دارُ العذابِ بجميع طبقاتها السبع التي أعلاها جهنّم (٢) ، وتحتها لَظَى ، ثُمَّ الحُطَمَة ، ثُمَّ السَّعيرُ ، ثُمَّ سَقَر ، ثُمَّ الجَحِيمُ ، ثُمَّ الهَاوِيَة ، وبابُ كلّ واحدة (٣) من داخل الأخرى على الاستواء، وبين أعلى جهنّم وأسفلها خمس وسبعمئة سنة ، وحَرُّها (٤) هواءٌ مُحرِقٌ ، ولا جَمر لها سوى بني آدم والأحجار المُتَّخَذَةِ آلِهَةٌ مِن دون الله .
وذكر ابن العربي (٥) أنَّ هذه النار التي في الدُّنيا ما أخرجها الله إلى النَّاسِ مِن جهنّم حتَّى غُسِلتْ في البحر مرَّتين، ولولا ذلك لم يُنتفع بها مِن حرّها ، وكفى بهذا زاجرا (١).
The obligation of belief in Paradise and Hell and their eternal existence according to what is known in detail or in summary, while negating the need for them or futility (upon the responsible human), its ultimate aim is that belief in them is devotional.
109. And Hell is true, created like Paradise, so do not incline to a denier who is insane.
(And Hell is true) i.e. established by the Book, the Sunnah, and the consensus of the scholars of the community, and everything that is like that... then belief in it is obligatory; this is the position of the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah. The intended meaning of "Fire" is the abode of punishment with all its seven layers, the highest of which is Jahannam, beneath it Ladha, then al-Hutama, then al-Sa'ir, then Saqar, then al-Jahim, then al-Hawiya. The door of each one is inside the other on the same level, and between the top of Jahannam and its bottom is five hundred and seventy years. Its heat is burning air, and it has no embers except for the children of Adam and the stones taken as gods besides Allah.
And Ibn al-Arabi mentioned that this Fire which is in the world, Allah brought it out from Jahannam to the people, then it was washed in the sea twice, and were it not for that, no benefit would be derived from it due to its heat, and this is sufficient as a deterrent.
Source pages p. 546

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the doctrine regarding Hell. It begins by stating the obligation of belief in Paradise and Hell and their eternal existence, whether known in detail or in summary, emphasizing that the purpose is devotional. Then it presents verse 109 of the poem: 'And Hell is true, created like Paradise, so do not incline to a denier who is insane.' The commentary follows: 'And Hell is true' means it is established by the Book, Sunnah, and consensus; belief in it is obligatory according to the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah. The term 'Fire' refers to the abode of punishment with its seven layers: Jahannam (uppermost), then Ladha, al-Hutama, al-Sa'ir, Saqar, al-Jahim, al-Hawiya. Each layer's door is inside the other on the same level. The distance between the top of Jahannam and its bottom is five hundred and seventy years. Its heat is burning air, and its fuel consists only of humans and stones that were worshipped as gods besides Allah. Finally, a report from Ibn al-Arabi is mentioned: the fire of this world was originally taken from Jahannam and washed twice in the sea, without which it could not be used—this serves as a deterrent.

Correction: The passage affirms that Hell is true and created (أُوجِدَت), established by revelation and consensus, and its seven layers are literal.

?

Refutation of Deniers of Creation of Paradise and Hell
Refutation of Mu'tazila using Qur'anic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are already created now, based on the Qur'anic word 'أوجِدَت', and how the Mu'tazila's view is refuted.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are created now, not merely future realities.

Before describing Paradise itself, the commentator first addresses a key doctrinal dispute: whether Paradise and Hell are already created. The Mu'tazila argued they will be created only on the Day of Recompense. The commentator uses the Qur'anic word 'أوجِدَت' (created) to affirm their present existence. Let's see how this refutation is made.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the structure: identification of the refuted group, the evidence, and the conclusion.
The passage begins by stating 'الرَّدُ على القائلين...' (The refutation of those who say...).
2
Identify the refuted group
The passage targets the Mu'tazila, who deny the present existence of Paradise and Hell. Understand their position: they believe these will be created only on the Day of Judgment.
3
Analyze the evidence
The key evidence is the Qur'anic word 'أوجِدَت' (created) from the verse about Hell. The commentator argues this indicates sensible creation at the time of revelation, hence Paradise and Hell already exist.
The passage also mentions the comparison 'كَالجَنَّةِ' (like Paradise) to affirm the reality of both.
4
Understand the refutation's significance
This refutation establishes that the afterlife's abodes are real, created entities, not metaphors or future creations. This is a foundational point for eschatological beliefs.
The refutation is based on a direct scriptural argument, showing the importance of Qur'anic wording in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرَّدُ على القائلينَ بعدم خَلْق الجنَّة والنار الآن
بجميع
ورَدَّ بقوله : (أُوجِدَتْ) الآن حسّا ، على المعتزلة القائلين بعدم وجودها الآن ، وإنَّما تُوجَد يومَ الجَزاء ، وقوله (كَالجَنَّةِ) تشبيه في الحقيَّة (٢) والإيجادِ فيما مضى (٣) ، والجَنَّة لغة : البُستان ، والمُراد منها عُرفًا: دار الثَّواب أنواعها ، وهل هي سبع جنّات متجاورة (٤) ؟ أوسطها وأفضلُهَا الفِردَوسُ ، وهو أعلَاهَا ، وفوقها عرش الرَّحمن ، ومنها تُفجِّر أنهار الجَنَّة ، وجنَّة المأوى(ه) ، وجنَّة الخُلد ، وجنَّة النَّعيم ، وجنَّة عَدْن ، ودار السلام، ودار الجلال، كما
The refutation of those who say that Paradise and Hell are not created now.
He refutes by His saying: "Created" now sensibly, against the Mu'tazila who say they do not exist now, rather they will exist on the Day of Recompense. And His saying "like Paradise" is a comparison in reality and in existence in the past. And "Jannah" linguistically means garden, and its customary intended meaning is the abode of reward; its types: are they seven adjacent gardens? Its middle and best is al-Firdaws, and it is the highest of them, above it is the Throne of the All-Merciful, and from it the rivers of Paradise spring forth. And Jannat al-Ma'wa, and Jannat al-Khuld, and Jannat al-Na'im, and Jannat 'Adn, and Dar al-Salam, and Dar al-Jalal, as...
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and a definition. It first refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that Paradise and Hell are not yet created but will be created on the Day of Recompense. The refutation uses the word 'أوجِدَت' (created) from the verse, which indicates that Hell (and by implication Paradise) has already been brought into existence sensibly. The comparison 'like Paradise' in the verse affirms that both are created and real. Then the passage defines 'Jannah' linguistically as 'garden' and technically as the abode of reward. It then discusses whether there are seven adjacent gardens; the best and highest is al-Firdaws, above which is the Throne of the Merciful, and from it the rivers of Paradise spring. It names several gardens: Jannat al-Ma'wa, Jannat al-Khuld, Jannat al-Na'im, Jannat 'Adn, Dar al-Salam, and Dar al-Jalal. The text ends with 'as...' indicating the continuation.

Key Terms
أوجِدَت
الجنة
النار
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Paradise and Hell are not yet created but will be created on the Day of Recompense.
Correction: The Qur'an uses the word 'أوجِدَت' (created) for Hell, indicating it already exists. Similarly, comparisons like 'like Paradise' show both are real and created now.

Checkpoint
Which group is refuted by the word 'أوجِدَت' according to this passage?
A) The Jahmiyyah
B) The Mu'tazila
C) The Khawarij
D) The Shi'a

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are already created, as proven by the Qur'anic word 'أوجِدَت', refuting the Mu'tazila.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live with a vivid awareness that Paradise and Hell are real and already exist, or do you treat them as distant future events? How would your daily choices change if you truly believe they are created now?
?
If the Mu'tazila are wrong, what about your own heart? Are there aspects of the unseen that you relegate to 'someday' instead of embracing as present truths? Will you today recite the Quranic evidence and let it transform your certainty?
?
The author refutes a sect, but do you ever act as though Paradise and Hell are not yet real? Imagine standing in front of the Prophet ﷺ and hearing him confirm they are created now. What would you do differently starting tomorrow?

Description of Paradise and Its Gardens
Definition and enumeration of Paradise's gardens.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different names and levels of Paradise, especially the highest garden al-Firdaws, and its relationship to the Throne and rivers.

Core Idea
Paradise has multiple gardens, the highest being al-Firdaws, from which the rivers flow.

Having established that Paradise is created now, the commentator turns to its description. He defines 'Jannah' linguistically and as the abode of reward, then discusses the number and hierarchy of its gardens. The highest and best is al-Firdaws, located beneath the Throne and source of Paradise's rivers.

Guided Path
1
Read the descriptive passage
Read the Arabic passage describing Paradise, focusing on the definition and enumeration of gardens.
The passage begins 'والجَنَّة لغة : البُستان' (Jannah linguistically means garden).
2
Understand the definition
Note the linguistic meaning ('garden') and the customary technical meaning ('abode of reward'). This sets the stage for describing its types.
3
List the gardens
The passage mentions several gardens: al-Firdaws, Jannat al-Ma'wa, Jannat al-Khuld, etc. Identify them and note the question of whether there are seven adjacent gardens.
The text raises the question: are there seven adjacent gardens?
4
Focus on al-Firdaws
Al-Firdaws is said to be the middle and best, the highest, above it is the Throne of the Merciful, and from it rivers spring. Understand its special status.
The Throne (عرش الرحمن) is above Firdaws, indicating its lofty position.
5
Reflect on the names
Each garden name (e.g., Jannat al-Khuld, Dar al-Salam) reflects a quality of Paradise. Consider the significance of these names.
The passage ends with 'كما' suggesting continuation, so we have only part of the description.

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and a definition. It first refutes the Mu'tazilite claim that Paradise and Hell are not yet created but will be created on the Day of Recompense. The refutation uses the word 'أوجِدَت' (created) from the verse, which indicates that Hell (and by implication Paradise) has already been brought into existence sensibly. The comparison 'like Paradise' in the verse affirms that both are created and real. Then the passage defines 'Jannah' linguistically as 'garden' and technically as the abode of reward. It then discusses whether there are seven adjacent gardens; the best and highest is al-Firdaws, above which is the Throne of the Merciful, and from it the rivers of Paradise spring. It names several gardens: Jannat al-Ma'wa, Jannat al-Khuld, Jannat al-Na'im, Jannat 'Adn, Dar al-Salam, and Dar al-Jalal. The text ends with 'as...' indicating the continuation.

Refuting Mu'tazila Denial of Paradise and Hell's Present Existence
Sanusi refutes Mu'tazila denial of Paradise and Hell's present existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are already created and exist now, contrary to the Mu'tazila belief.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now, created by Allah.

Sanusi addresses a key dispute about when Paradise and Hell exist. The Mu'tazila argue they will be created only on the Day of Judgment, but the Ash'ari position affirms their present, sensible existence. This passage defends that view and clarifies the meaning of Paradise.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage

The passage is short but packed with doctrinal meaning.
2
Identify the refuted group
The Mu'tazila are identified as denying the current existence of Paradise and Hell. Understand their position: they believe these will be created on the Day of Recompense.
3
Examine the linguistic clarification
Sanusi explains that 'Paradise' linguistically means 'garden' and technically refers to the abode of reward. This reinforces the physical reality of Paradise.
This definition counters any allegorical interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورَدَّ بقوله : (أُوجِدَتْ) الآن حسّا ، على المعتزلة القائلين بعدم وجودها الآن ، وإنَّما تُوجَد يومَ الجَزاء ، وقوله (كَالجَنَّةِ) تشبيه في الحقيَّة (٢) والإيجادِ فيما مضى (۳) ، والجَنَّة لغة : البُستان ، والمُراد منها عُرفًا: دار الثَّواب أنواعها

Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who deny the current existence of Paradise and Hell, claiming they will only be created on the Day of Judgment. The author states that the phrase 'it was created' in the poem affirms their present, sensible existence. The Mu'tazila are refuted because they restrict existence to the future. The author then explains the simile 'like Paradise' in the text, noting it is a comparison in reality and past creation. Finally, he defines Paradise linguistically ('garden') and technically ('abode of reward'), encompassing all its types.

How Many Gardens? The Debate on Paradise
Sanusi enumerates three scholarly opinions on the number of gardens.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing scholarly views on the number of gardens (Paradises) and the evidence each view relies on.

Core Idea
The garden's names describe one reality, not separate places.

Sanusi presents three opinions on the number of gardens: seven, four, or one. This debate is not about the existence of Paradise but about how to interpret the various names given in the Qur'an and hadith. The passage shows how scholars derive their views from scriptural evidence and conceptual reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the footnote markers in the Arabic text.
2
Identify the three views
The passage presents three opinions. Find each one and note the evidence provided for it. The views are: seven gardens, four gardens, and one garden.
3
Examine the evidence for each view
For the seven-garden view, Ibn 'Abbas is cited. For the four-garden view, Quranic verses (55:46 and 55:62) are used. For the one-garden view, the majority argue that the names are attributes of a single garden.
4
Understand the reasoning behind the majority view
The majority view relies on the idea that all names (like 'Adn, Khuld, etc.) describe characteristics—permanence, safety, bliss—that can all apply to one garden.
5
Reflect on the significance of the debate
Consider why this debate matters. It shows how scholars interpret scriptural names and whether they designate distinct entities or attributes of a single reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهل هي سبع جنّات متجاورة (٤) ؟ أوسطها وأفضلُهَا الفِردَوسُ ، وهو أعلَاهَا ، وفوقها عرش الرَّحمن ، ومنها تُفجِّر أنهار الجَنَّة ، وجنَّة المأوى(ه) ، وجنَّة الخُلد ، وجنَّة النَّعيم ، وجنَّة عَدْن ، ودار السلام، ودار الجلال، كما ذهب إليه ابن عبّاس ، أو أربع (۱) ، ورجّحه جماعةٌ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِمَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِ جَنَّتَانِ ﴾ [الرحمن : ٤٦] . ثمَّ قال: ﴿وَمِن دُونِهِمَا جَنَّتَانِ ﴾ [الرحمن : ٦٢] . كما ذهب إليه الجمهور ، أو واحدة والأسماء والصفات كُلُّها جاريةٌ عليها لتحقق معانيها كُلّها فيها ؛ إذْ يَصدقُ على الجميع (۲): جنَّة عَدْنٍ، أي: إقامة ، كما أنَّها كلّها مأوى المؤمنين ، وكذلك دار الخلد ، ودار السلام، لأنَّ جميعها للخلود والسَّلامة مِن كُلِّ خَوفٍ وحزن ، وجنَّة نعيم؛ لأنَّها كلّها مَشحُونة بأصنافه.
And is it seven adjacent gardens? Their middle and best is al-Firdaws, and it is the highest of them, and above it is the Throne of the Merciful, and from it the rivers of Paradise gush forth, and Jannat al-Ma'wa, and Jannat al-Khuld, and Jannat al-Na'im, and Jannat 'Adn, and Dar al-Salam, and Dar al-Jalal, as held by Ibn 'Abbas, or four, and a group preferred it due to His saying: 'And for him who fears the standing before his Lord are two gardens' [55:46], then He said: 'And besides these two are two gardens' [55:62], as held by the majority, or one, and all the names and attributes apply to it due to the realization of all their meanings in it; for it is all called Jannat 'Adn, i.e. permanent abode, just as it is all the abode of the believers, and likewise Dar al-Khuld and Dar al-Salam, because all of them are for eternity and safety from every fear and grief, and Jannat Na'im, because all are filled with its kinds.
Source pages p. 547

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the differing views on the number of gardens (Paradises). The author presents three opinions: (1) Seven gardens that are adjacent, with al-Firdaws as the highest and middle, above which is the Throne of the Merciful, and from which the rivers flow; this view is attributed to Ibn 'Abbas. (2) Four gardens, preferred by a group based on the Quranic verses mentioning two gardens and then two other gardens. (3) One garden with multiple names and attributes, as held by the majority (جمهور); all the names like 'Adn, Khuld, etc., apply because they describe its characteristics—permanence, safety, bliss—and all are realized in it. The author does not explicitly endorse any view but presents them as scholarly positions.

Key Terms
جنّات
الفردوس
عرش الرَّحمن
ابن عباس
جمهور
جنّة عَدْن
دار السلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think there are multiple separate gardens and the debate is about which one is correct.
Correction: The debate is about how to interpret the names—whether they designate separate gardens or attributes of one garden.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which view holds that the names and attributes of Paradise all apply to a single garden?
A) The view of Ibn 'Abbas.
B) The view preferred by a group based on Quran verses.
C) The view of the majority (جمهور).
D) The view of the Mu'tazila.

Key Takeaway
Whether viewed as one or many, the names of Paradise describe its perfections, not distinct locations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The verse 'And for him who fears the standing before his Lord are two gardens' promises Paradise to those who fear standing before Allah. Do you genuinely fear that moment, or does it slip your mind? What would it take for you to live with that fear turning you into action?
?
The majority view says all names describe one essential reality. This means Paradise is not fragmented but a perfect whole. Are you pursuing a fragmented version of the Hereafter—wanting some parts but ignoring others—or do you desire the full reality of what Allah has prepared, in all its aspects?

Proof for Current Existence of Paradise and Hell from Adam's Story
Sanusi provides evidence from Adam's story and warns against denying their present existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural and consensus-based evidence for the present existence of Paradise and Hell, and the gravity of denying their existence.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now; denying this is disbelief or innovation.

Imam Sanusi provides a decisive proof from the story of Adam and Eve being placed in Paradise. He cites the Quran, Sunnah, and consensus. He then warns against those who deny their present existence, distinguishing between total denial (philosophers) and denial of current existence (Mu'tazilites). This lesson unpacks the evidence and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once without translating. Focus on the flow: proof, then warning.
2
Identify the proof from Adam's story
Notice how Sanusi uses the story to establish the existence of Paradise and Hell. Also note the consensus and explicit Quranic verses.
The proof relies on both revelation and scholarly consensus.
3
Understand the range of deniers
Sanusi distinguishes between philosophers (complete denial) and Mu'tazilites (denial of current existence). Understand the different rulings for each.
Complete denial is disbelief; denial of present existence is innovation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والدليل لنا على ثبوتهما قِصَّةُ آدم وحواء ، وإسكانهما الجنَّة ، على ما جاء به القُرآن والسُّنَّة ، وانعقد عليه الإجماع قبل ظهور المُخالف ، ولا قائل بخلق الجنَّة دونَ النَّار ؛ فثبوتها ثبوتها (۳) ، والآيات صريحة في ذلك، وقد أجمعَ العلماء على أنَّ تأويلها (٤) من غير ضرورة إلحاد في الدين، والجنَّة فوقَ السَّموات السبع ، ولم يَصِحَ في محلّ النَّارِ خَبْرُ . (فَلَا تَمِلْ) أي: لا تُصْغِ بعد جزمِك بحقيتهما ووجودهما الآنَ الواجِبِ عليكَ (لِجَاحِدٍ) ، أي : لِقولِ مُنكِرهِما بالمرَّة كالفلاسفة ؛ لكفره ، أو لقول منكر وجودهما الآنَ كأبي هاشم (٥) وعبد الجبار (1) المعتزليين؛ لتبديعه (ذِي جِنَّةِ)
And the proof for us of their existence is the story of Adam and Eve, and their settling in Paradise, according to what the Quran and Sunnah have brought, and consensus was concluded upon it before the appearance of the opponent. And no one says that Paradise is created without the Fire; so its establishment is its establishment. And the verses are explicit in that, and the scholars have agreed that its interpretation without necessity is heresy in religion. And Paradise is above the seven heavens, and no report has been confirmed about the location of the Fire. So do not incline, i.e., do not listen after your certainty of their reality and their existence now, which is obligatory upon you, to a denier, i.e., to the statement of one who rejects them entirely like the philosophers, due to his disbelief, or to the statement of one who rejects their existence now like Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar the Mu'tazilites, due to his innovation, of madness.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for the current existence of Paradise and Hell from the story of Adam and Eve being placed in Paradise, as narrated in the Quran and Sunnah. The author emphasizes that there was consensus on this before the emergence of opponents, and no one differentiates by creating Paradise without Hell. The verses are explicit, and interpreting them without necessity is considered heresy. He then states that Paradise is above the seven heavens, while no authentic report specifies Hell's location. After this, the author warns the reader not to incline to any denier: whether a philosopher who rejects both entirely (disbelief) or a Mu'tazilite like Abu Hashim and 'Abd al-Jabbar who deny their current existence (innovation). The passage concludes with a remark perhaps implying such denial stems from madness.

Key Terms
قِصَّة آدم وحواء
الإجماع
الفلاسفة
أبو هاشم
عبد الجبار
تبديعه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Denying the current existence of Paradise and Hell is a minor doctrinal error.
Correction: Sanusi warns that complete denial is disbelief and denial of present existence is innovation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on one who denies the existence of Paradise and Hell entirely?
A) He is an innovator (mubtadi').
B) He is a disbeliever (kafir).
C) He is mistaken but still a believer.
D) He is a Mu'tazilite.

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell exist now; denying that is a serious error—either disbelief or innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that Paradise and Hell exist right now, at this very moment—or is it just a distant future hope? If you lived with that certainty, what would change in your choices today?
?
Sanusi warns you not to incline to any denier, not even a moment of doubt. Search your heart: have you ever allowed the whispers of philosophers or modern skeptics to weaken your conviction about the reality of the Hereafter? What step will you take to fortify that certainty?
?
Adam was placed in a real, existing Paradise—a garden that is still there today. You are not Adam, but your destiny hangs on the same reality. Are you living as someone who is preparing to enter that Paradise, or are you distracted as if it does not exist? What is the one change you will make this week to prove you believe it?

Refutation of the Denial of Paradise and Hell's Current Creation
The author refutes the claim that Paradise and Hell are not created now, citing evidence from the story of Adam and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence from Adam's story and scholarly consensus that proves Paradise and Hell are created now.

Core Idea
Adam's dwelling in Paradise proves it was created; consensus confirms Hell's creation.

Some have claimed that Paradise and Hell are not yet created. The author refutes this by pointing to the clear story of Adam and Eve living in Paradise, which is affirmed by the Qur'an and Sunnah, and by the consensus of scholars before any dissenter appeared. This lesson examines that evidence and clarifies that both Paradise and Hell are existing creations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the claim
Begin by reading the Arabic and English translation. Note that the passage starts by stating it is a refutation of those who say Paradise and Hell are not created now.
The claim being refuted is the central issue.
2
Understand the two views on Paradise
The passage mentions two opinions: one attributed to Ibn Abbas (or four) and the majority view. Notice how the author uses Quranic verses from Surat Ar-Rahman to support different numbers of gardens.
These views are not the main evidence but show diversity of interpretation.
3
Grasp the primary evidence from Adam and Eve
Focus on the sentence starting with 'And the evidence for us...' The author cites the story of Adam and Eve dwelling in the Garden, as per Quran and Sunnah, and the consensus before any dissenter appeared.
This is the core proof: historical event and scholarly agreement.
4
Reflect on the conclusion and location
Note that the author argues no one claims the Garden is created without the Fire, so both must exist. Also learn that Paradise is above the seven heavens, while no authentic report exists for Hell's location.
The location detail is peripheral but confirms creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرَّدُ على القائلينَ بعدم خَلْق الجنَّة والنار الآن • ذهب إليه ابن عبّاس ، أو أربع (۱) ، ورجّحه جماعةٌ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِمَنْ خَافَ مَقَامَ رَبِّهِ جَنَّتَانِ ﴾ [الرحمن : ٤٦] . ثمَّ قال: ﴿وَمِن دُونِهِمَا جَنَّتَانِ ﴾ [الرحمن : ٦٢] . كما ذهب إليه الجمهور ، أو واحدة والأسماء والصفات كُلُّها جاريةٌ عليها لتحقق معانيها كُلّها فيها ؛ إذْ يَصدقُ على الجميع (۲): جنَّة عَدْنٍ، أي: إقامة ، كما أنَّها كلّها مأوى المؤمنين ، وكذلك دار الخلد ، ودار السلام، لأنَّ جميعها للخلود والسَّلامة مِن كُلِّ خَوفٍ وحزن ، وجنَّة نعيم؛ لأنَّها كلّها مَشحُونة بأصنافه. : والدليل لنا على ثبوتهما قِصَّةُ آدم وحواء ، وإسكانهما الجنَّة ، على ما جاء به القُرآن والسُّنَّة ، وانعقد عليه الإجماع قبل ظهور المُخالف ، ولا قائل بخلق الجنَّة دونَ النَّار ؛ فثبوتها ثبوتها (۳) ، والآيات صريحة في ذلك، وقد أجمعَ العلماء على أنَّ تأويلها (٤) من غير ضرورة إلحاد في الدين، والجنَّة فوقَ السَّموات السبع ، ولم يَصِحَ في محلّ النَّارِ خَبْرُ .
The refutation of those who say that Paradise and Hell are not created now. Ibn Abbas held this opinion, or four (1), and a group preferred it due to His statement: 'But for he who has feared the standing of his Lord are two gardens' [Ar-Rahman 46]. Then He said: 'And besides these two are two [other] gardens' [Ar-Rahman 62]. As the majority held, or one, and all the names and attributes apply to it because all their meanings are realized in it; for it is true of all (2): Garden of Eden, i.e., a place of residence, just as all of them are the abode of the believers, and likewise the Abode of Eternity and the Abode of Peace, because all of them are for eternity and safety from every fear and sorrow, and Garden of Bliss, because all of them are filled with its varieties. And the evidence for us of their existence is the story of Adam and Eve and their dwelling in the Garden, according to what the Qur'an and Sunnah brought, and consensus was established upon it before the emergence of the dissenter. And no one says that the Garden is created without the Fire; so their existence is their existence (3). And the verses are explicit about that, and the scholars have agreed that interpreting them (4) without necessity is atheism in religion. And the Garden is above the seven heavens, and no authentic report has been established about the location of the Fire.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who claim that Paradise and Hell are not currently created. It begins by presenting two views on the number of gardens mentioned in the Quran: one attributed to Ibn Abbas (or four) and the majority view. The author then notes that all the names of Paradise (e.g., Garden of Eden, Abode of Eternity) apply to it collectively because their meanings are realized. The main evidence presented is the story of Adam and Eve dwelling in Paradise, which is supported by Quran and Sunnah, and the consensus (ijma) that existed before any dissenter appeared. The author emphasizes that no one claims the Garden is created without the Fire, so they are both created. The passage ends by stating that Paradise is located above the seven heavens, while no authentic report exists for the location of Hell.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Paradise and Hell are not yet created; they will be created only after Judgment Day.
Correction: The Qur'an and Sunnah show that Paradise was created for Adam, and scholarly consensus confirms that both are created now.

Checkpoint

A) The majority opinion of scholars
B) The story of Adam and Eve and consensus before dissenters
C) The names of Paradise imply eternity

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are already created, as proven by the story of Adam and the consensus of scholars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If Hell is already burning, what does that tell you about the weight of your words and actions right now—especially those no one sees? Will you let that reality pierce your comfort?
?
The author calls interpreting clear verses without necessity 'atheism in religion.' When you read the descriptions of Paradise and Hell, do you allow them to move you deeply, or do you rationalize them away? What is one thing you can change today to make that reality more vivid in your life?

The Danger of Denying Paradise and Hell
Warning against heeding deniers of Paradise and Hell, with a twofold classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification of deniers of Paradise and Hell as either disbelievers or innovators, and why denying their current existence leads to rejecting necessary religious knowledge.

Core Idea
Denying any aspect of Paradise and Hell is a dangerous path to madness.

This lesson unpacks the author's stern warning against listening to those who deny the reality of Paradise and Hell, whether they deny them entirely or only their current existence. The author makes a sharp distinction between disbelief and innovation, reminding the student of the severe consequences of such denial.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb its rhythm, then read the literal translation. Notice the direct command at the start.
2
Identify the two categories of deniers
The passage mentions two types: total deniers (philosophers) and those denying only current existence (Mu'tazila). Note the different rulings for each.
Philosophers are disbelievers; Mu'tazila are innovators.
3
Understand the gravity of denial
The author calls such a denier 'possessed of madness' because their denial leads to rejecting what is known necessarily from religion.
This shows the severity of even partial denial.
4
Reflect on the necessity of affirmation
The author implies that affirming the reality and current existence of Paradise and Hell is obligatory knowledge from the religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(فَلَا تَمِلْ) أي: لا تُصْغِ بعد جزمِك بحقيتهما ووجودهما الآنَ الواجِبِ عليكَ (لِجَاحِدٍ) ، أي : لِقولِ مُنكِرهِما بالمرَّة كالفلاسفة ؛ لكفره ، أو لقول منكر وجودهما الآنَ كأبي هاشم (٥) وعبد الجبار (1) المعتزليين; لتبديعه (ذِي جِنَّةِ) أي: صاحبِ جُنونٍ ؛ لأنَّ إنكارَهُمَا وما عُلِّلَ به.. يؤدي إلى إحالة ما عُلم مِن الدين ضرورة.
('So do not incline') i.e., do not listen, after your certainty of their reality and their current existence, which is obligatory upon you, (to a denier), i.e., to the statement of one who denies them entirely, like the philosophers, due to his disbelief, or to the statement of one who denies their current existence, like Abu Hashim (5) and Abd al-Jabbar (1) of the Mu'tazila, due to his innovation. (Possessed of madness) i.e., a madman, because their denial and what is reasoned with it leads to rejecting what is known of religion by necessity.
Source pages p. 548

Commentary
This passage is a warning against heeding deniers of the current existence of Paradise and Hell. The author interprets the phrase 'fala tamil' as an imperative: 'do not incline' or 'do not listen' after one has become certain of their reality and existence, which is obligatory. The author classifies deniers into two types: those who deny both entirely, like the philosophers, which is disbelief; and those who deny only their current existence, like the Mu'tazili scholars Abu Hashim and Abd al-Jabbar, which is innovation (bid'a). The author then calls such a denier 'possessed of madness' (dhi jinnah), because their denial leads to rejecting what is known necessarily (darurah) from religion.

Key Terms

فلاسفة
أبو هاشم
عبد الجبار
معتزلة
جِنَّة
الضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that denying the current existence of Paradise and Hell is a minor theological disagreement without serious consequences.
Correction: The author states it leads to rejecting necessary religious knowledge, deeming such a person mad and their position a dangerous innovation.

Checkpoint
How does the author classify those who deny the current existence of Paradise and Hell?
A) All are disbelievers
B) Philosophers are disbelievers; those denying current existence are innovators
C) All are considered mad
D) Only philosophers are innovators

Key Takeaway
The author's warning is clear: denying Paradise and Hell, in whole or part, is dangerous and leads to rejecting necessary religious truths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself downplaying the reality of Paradise and Hell in your daily life, as if they are distant or metaphorical? What does the author's warning about 'inclining' to deniers reveal about the state of your own heart? Commit today to renew your certainty by reciting the Quranic descriptions of the Hereafter.
?
Think of someone—a scholar, friend, or social media figure—whose views on the afterlife seem lenient or dismissive. Are you tempted to excuse them because of their intellect or sincerity? The author calls such deniers 'mad'—does your comfort with their ideas reflect a lack of urgency in your own faith? Will you distance yourself from their influence?
?
The passage demands absolute certainty (jazm) in the current existence of Paradise and Hell. Is your certainty at that level? If not, what is holding you back? What one specific action can you take this week to strengthen your conviction in the unseen—such as studying the proofs or reflecting on the temporary nature of this world?

Refuting the Jahmiyya: Eternity of Paradise and Hell
Refutes Jahmiyya and defines blessed/wretched with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core refutation of the Jahmiyya denial of the eternity of Paradise and Hell, and the definition of the blessed and wretched based on one's state at death.

Core Idea
The final abode is determined by the state at death, not by past deeds.

This lesson addresses a critical theological deviation: the Jahmiyya claim that Paradise and Hell will one day end. The author firmly refutes this by affirming both as eternal abodes. He then defines who are the blessed and the wretched, clarifying that what matters is one's final state—dying upon faith or disbelief. This sets the foundation for understanding divine justice and the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of the Jahmiyya
Carefully read the opening sentence where the author rejects the Jahmiyya position on the perishing of Paradise and Hell. Note the basis for refutation: opposition to Quran and Sunnah.
The Jahmiyya sect held extreme theological views; their denial of eternal punishment was a major deviation.
2
Understand the definitions of sa'id and shaqi
Identify how the author defines the 'blessed' (sa'id) and 'wretched' (shaqi). Note that the definition hinges entirely on the state at death, not on prior actions.
3
Reflect on the Quranic proof
Examine the proof from Surah Hud 11:105, which mentions 'wretched and blessed.' Consider how this verse supports the author's definitions and counters the Jahmiyya.
The verse is used as direct evidence for the classification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَرَدَّ بِقَوْلِهِ: (دَارَا) خُلُودٍ)، أَيْ: إِقَامَةٌ مُؤَيَّدَةٌ، عَلَى الْجَهْمِيَّةِ الْقَائِلِينَ بِفَنَائِهِمَا وَفَنَاءِ أَهْلِهِمَا، لِمُخَالَفَتِهِ الْكِتَابَ وَالسُّنَّةَ. فَالْجَنَّةُ دَارُ خُلُودٍ (لِلسَّعِيدِ) أَيِ: الَّذِي مَاتَ عَلَى الْإِسْلَامِ وَإِنْ تَقَدَّمَ مِنْهُ كُفْرٌ، (وَ) النَّارُ دَارُ خُلُودِ (الشَّقِيِّ) الَّذِي مَاتَ عَلَى الْكُفْرِ وَإِنْ عَاشَ طُولَ عُمُرِهِ عَلَى الْإِيمَانِ؛ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ شَقِيٌّ وَسَعِيدٌ﴾ [هود: 105] الْآيَةَ. وَدَخَلَ فِي الشَّقِيِّ: الْكَافِرُ الْجَاهِلُ، وَالْمُعَانِدُ، وَمَنْ بَالَغَ فِي النَّظَرِ فَلَمْ يَصِلْ إِلَى الْحَقِّ، وَلَا يَدْخُلُ فِيهِ أَطْفَالُ الْمُشْرِكِينَ، بَلْ هُمْ فِي الْجَنَّةِ عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ، وَأَمَّا أَطْفَالُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فَفِي الْجَنَّةِ عِنْدَ الْجُمْهُورِ، وَأَمَّا أَوْلَادُ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ فَفِي الْجَنَّةِ إِجْمَاعًا. وَيَدْخُلُ فِي السَّعِيدِ وَالشَّقِيِّ مَنْ كَانَ مِنَ الْجِنِّ كَذَلِكَ.
And he refuted by his saying: 'two abodes of eternity', i.e., an everlasting abode, against the Jahmiyya who say that they (Paradise and Hell) and their inhabitants will perish, due to their opposition to the Book and the Sunnah. So Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed one, meaning: the one who died upon Islam even if disbelief preceded from him; and the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched one, the one who died upon disbelief even if he lived his entire life upon faith; due to His saying, exalted: 'And among them are wretched and blessed' [Hud 11:105] the verse. And included in the wretched are: the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate, and the one who exerted himself in inquiry but did not arrive at the truth. And the children of the polytheists are not included in it; rather they are in Paradise according to the correct view. As for the children of the believers, they are in Paradise according to the majority. And as for the children of the prophets, they are in Paradise by consensus. And included in the blessed and the wretched are those who are from the jinn likewise.
Source pages p. 549

Commentary
This passage is a definition and refutation. The author refutes the Jahmiyya sect, which claimed that Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants will eventually perish, arguing that this contradicts the Quran and Sunnah. He then defines the 'blessed' (sa'id) as one who dies in a state of Islam, even if he had previously committed disbelief or sins; and the 'wretched' (shaqi) as one who dies in a state of disbelief, even if he lived most of his life as a believer. The proof cited is Quran 11:105. The author then expands on who falls under 'wretched': the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate denier, and the one who exerted himself in intellectual inquiry but failed to reach the truth. Importantly, children of polytheists are excluded; they are in Paradise according to the correct position. Children of believers are in Paradise according to the majority, and children of prophets are in Paradise by consensus. Finally, the same classification applies to jinn, who are also included among the blessed and wretched.

Key Terms
السعيد
الشقي
الجهمية
دار الخلود

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that past sins or disbelief affect the final abode even if one later repents and dies a Muslim.
Correction: The passage clarifies that what matters is the state at the moment of death; even a lifetime of disbelief is erased by dying upon faith, and a lifetime of faith is negated by dying upon disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is considered 'blessed' (sa'id)?
A) One who never committed any sin
B) One who died upon Islam even if disbelief preceded
C) One who performed many good deeds
D) One who was born a Muslim

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are eternal, and one's final abode depends solely on the state of faith or disbelief at death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die this moment, would you be counted among the blessed or the wretched? What in your life right now gives you that certainty?
?
Do you rely on past good deeds or a time of faith that has passed, while neglecting your current state? How can you ensure you are on the path of the blessed right now?
?
The Jahmiyya's claim that Paradise and Hell will perish takes away the weight of eternity. Have you ever acted as if the consequences of your actions are temporary? What would change if you truly lived with the certainty of an eternal abode?

Categories of the Wretched and Status of Children and Jinn
Enumerates types of wretched and rules on children and jinn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of the wretched, the fate of children of polytheists, believers, and prophets, and that jinn are included in the blessed and wretched.

Core Idea
The wretched include three types, but children are saved by default.

After the basic definitions, the author delves deeper into who is considered 'wretched'. He identifies three specific categories: the ignorant disbeliever, the obstinate, and the one who sincerely sought truth but failed to find it. He then addresses the fate of children, explaining that children of polytheists are in Paradise, and this is also the majority and consensus view for children of believers and prophets respectively. Finally, he extends the classification to the jinn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of the wretched
Read the list of three types included in 'wretched'. Notice the distinctions: ignorant disbeliever, obstinate denier, and the sincere seeker who did not reach the truth.
The third type is notable: it implies that even sincere effort without correct conclusion leads to wretchedness if they die in that state.
2
Understand the exception for children
Notice that children of polytheists are explicitly excluded from 'wretched'. Then see the three rulings: children of polytheists in Paradise (correct view), children of believers in Paradise (majority), children of prophets in Paradise (consensus).
This shows mercy to those who died before the age of accountability.
3
Consider the inclusion of jinn
Note that the author concludes by stating jinn are also included in the blessed and wretched, meaning the same classification applies to them.
This is an important extension of human theology to the jinn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَرَدَّ بِقَوْلِهِ: (دَارَا) خُلُودٍ)، أَيْ: إِقَامَةٌ مُؤَيَّدَةٌ، عَلَى الْجَهْمِيَّةِ الْقَائِلِينَ بِفَنَائِهِمَا وَفَنَاءِ أَهْلِهِمَا، لِمُخَالَفَتِهِ الْكِتَابَ وَالسُّنَّةَ. فَالْجَنَّةُ دَارُ خُلُودٍ (لِلسَّعِيدِ) أَيِ: الَّذِي مَاتَ عَلَى الْإِسْلَامِ وَإِنْ تَقَدَّمَ مِنْهُ كُفْرٌ، (وَ) النَّارُ دَارُ خُلُودِ (الشَّقِيِّ) الَّذِي مَاتَ عَلَى الْكُفْرِ وَإِنْ عَاشَ طُولَ عُمُرِهِ عَلَى الْإِيمَانِ؛ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: ﴿فَمِنْهُمْ شَقِيٌّ وَسَعِيدٌ﴾ [هود: 105] الْآيَةَ. وَدَخَلَ فِي الشَّقِيِّ: الْكَافِرُ الْجَاهِلُ، وَالْمُعَانِدُ، وَمَنْ بَالَغَ فِي النَّظَرِ فَلَمْ يَصِلْ إِلَى الْحَقِّ، وَلَا يَدْخُلُ فِيهِ أَطْفَالُ الْمُشْرِكِينَ، بَلْ هُمْ فِي الْجَنَّةِ عَلَى الصَّحِيحِ، وَأَمَّا أَطْفَالُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ فَفِي الْجَنَّةِ عِنْدَ الْجُمْهُورِ، وَأَمَّا أَوْلَادُ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ فَفِي الْجَنَّةِ إِجْمَاعًا. وَيَدْخُلُ فِي السَّعِيدِ وَالشَّقِيِّ مَنْ كَانَ مِنَ الْجِنِّ كَذَلِكَ.
And he refuted by his saying: 'two abodes of eternity', i.e., an everlasting abode, against the Jahmiyya who say that they (Paradise and Hell) and their inhabitants will perish, due to their opposition to the Book and the Sunnah. So Paradise is an abode of eternity for the blessed one, meaning: the one who died upon Islam even if disbelief preceded from him; and the Fire is an abode of eternity for the wretched one, the one who died upon disbelief even if he lived his entire life upon faith; due to His saying, exalted: 'And among them are wretched and blessed' [Hud 11:105] the verse. And the children of the polytheists are not included in it; rather they are in Paradise according to the correct view. As for the children of the believers, they are in Paradise according to the majority. And as for the children of the prophets, they are in Paradise by consensus. And included in the blessed and the wretched are those who are from the jinn likewise.

Commentary
This passage is a definition and refutation. The author refutes the Jahmiyya sect, which claimed that Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants will eventually perish, arguing that this contradicts the Quran and Sunnah. He then defines the 'blessed' (sa'id) as one who dies in a state of Islam, even if he had previously committed disbelief or sins; and the 'wretched' (shaqi) as one who dies in a state of disbelief, even if he lived most of his life as a believer. ?

Temporary Punishment of Sinful Muslims
Explains temporary punishment of sinful Muslims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that sinful Muslims are not eternally punished in Hell and that they die for a moment after entering before being taken out.

Core Idea
Sinful believers are not eternally punished; they die briefly then exit Hell.

This passage clarifies a key Sunni doctrine: the temporary nature of punishment for believers who enter Hell due to their sins. The author draws this from the poem's wording and explains the precise mechanism: a temporary death after entry, known only to God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow. Then read the translation carefully.
Notice how the author derives the ruling from the poem's arrangement.
2
Identify the central claim
Pinpoint the statement that sinful believers are not eternally punished. Understand the reasoning: because they are blessed, their eternal home is Paradise.
3
Understand the nuance of dying after entering
The author explains that they die after entering for a moment known only to God, then are taken out. This is not eternal punishment.
This distinguishes them from the eternally damned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعُلِمَ مِنَ النَّظْمِ أَنَّ عُصَاةَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ لَا يُخَلَّدُونَ فِي النَّارِ إِنْ دَخَلُوهَا؛ لِأَنَّهُمْ سُعَدَاءُ، فَدَارُ خُلُودِهِمُ الْجَنَّةُ. وَفُهِمَ مِنْ دَوَامِ عَذَابِ الْمُخَلَّدِينَ أَنَّ غَيْرَهُمْ لَا يَدُومُ عَذَابُهُ مُدَّةَ بَقَائِهِ، كَعُصَاةِ الْمُوَحِّدِينَ أَهْلِ الطَّبَقَةِ الْعُلْيَا، بَلْ يَمُوتُونَ بَعْدَ الدُّخُولِ لَحْظَةً مَا، يَعْلَمُ اللَّهُ مِقْدَارَهَا فَلَا يَحْيَوْنَ حَتَّى يُخْرَجُوا مِنْهَا. فَدَاخِلُ النَّارِ مَا (مُعَذَّبٌ) فِيهَا بِنَوْعٍ مِنْ أَنْوَاعِ عَذَابِهَا، أَوْ بِأَنْوَاعٍ مُتَعَدِّدَةٍ مِنْهُ مُدَّةَ بَقَائِهِ فِيهَا، وَدَاخِلُ الْجَنَّةِ (مُنَعَّمٌ) فِيهَا بِنَوْعٍ مِنْ أَنْوَاعِ نَعِيمِهَا، أَوْ بِأَنْوَاعٍ مُتَعَدِّدَةٍ مِنْهُ مُدَّةَ بَقَائِهِ فِيهَا. فَفِي الرَّدِّ عَلَى الْقَائِلِينَ بِعَدَمِ خَلْقِ الْجَنَّةِ وَالنَّارِ الْآنَ.
And it is understood from the arrangement (of the poem) that the disobedient among the believers are not eternally [fixed] in the Fire if they enter it; because they are blessed, so their abode of eternity is Paradise. And it is understood from the perpetuity of the punishment of the eternally [punished] that others' punishment does not last for the duration of their stay, like the disobedient monotheists, the people of the highest rank; rather they die after entering for a certain moment, the measure of which God knows, and they do not live until they are brought out of it. So the dweller of the Fire is (punished) therein with one of the types of its punishment, or with multiple types thereof, for the duration of his stay in it; and the dweller of Paradise is (blissful) therein with one of the types of its bliss, or with multiple types thereof, for the duration of his stay in it. So it is in refutation of those who say that Paradise and Fire are not created now.
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and refutation. It first derives from the poem's phrasing that sinful believers are not eternally punished in Hell, because they are essentially 'blessed' (sa'id) and their ultimate eternal abode is Paradise. The author then reasons that since the punishment of the eternally damned is perpetual, the punishment of others (i.e., sinful monotheists) does not last for their entire stay. Instead, they die after entering Hell for a brief moment known only to God, and then they are removed. The passage then describes the general state of all dwellers: those in Hell are punished, and those in Paradise are blissful, for the duration of their respective stays. Finally, the author presents this as a refutation of those who deny that Paradise and Hell have been created already, implying that the poem affirms their present existence.

Key Terms
عصاة المؤمنين
الخلود
الموت بعد الدخول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Sinful Muslims are eternally punished in Hell.
Correction: The passage states they are not eternally punished; they die briefly and are taken out, because they are ultimately blessed.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to sinful believers who enter Hell?
A) They are punished eternally like the deniers.
B) They die for a short time and then are taken out.
C) They never enter Hell at all.
D) They become permanently unconscious.

Key Takeaway
Sinful Muslims are not eternally punished; they die for a known moment after entering Hell and then are taken out to Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe you are still among the 'blessed' destined for Paradise? Or does your guilt make you doubt that God's mercy can still claim you? This lesson says you are not eternally lost—but are you using that as a license to sin, or as a reason to repent now, before you experience even a moment of that death in Hell?
?
Imagine standing at the edge of Hell, knowing you deserve punishment. This teaching says you would die after entering—but that moment of death is terrifyingly real. Are you relying on that momentary death to cleanse you, or are you actively seeking God's forgiveness today to minimize your time in that fire?
?
If you knew that every sin you commit will be met with a proportional moment of suffering in Hell, would you still cling to that sin? What is one sin you are unwilling to abandon, and why does your attachment to it outweigh the fear of that awful moment?

Refutation of Denial of Creation of Paradise and Hell
Refutes denial of current creation of Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell have already been created, based on the logical implications of the passage.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now, created by Allah.

The passage concludes with a refutation of those who deny that Paradise and Hell have been created. The author argues that because dwellers are punished or blissful for the duration of their stay, it follows that these abodes must exist presently.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice how the description of dwellers leads into the refutation.

Understand the description of dwellers
The author states that every dweller in Hell is punished with some type of punishment, and every dweller in Paradise is blissful with some type of bliss, for the entire duration of their stay.
This is a general characterization.
3
Connect to the refutation
The author directly states that this description serves as a refutation of those who say Paradise and Hell are not created now. The implication is that these abodes must already exist to be experienced.

5 min
The Creation of Paradise and Hell Now
Commentator affirms creation of Paradise and Hell now

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the majority of scholars affirm that Paradise and Hell are already created now, and that children of the Prophets are in Paradise by consensus, with the jinn included in the categories of happy and wretched.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now; good souls dwell there immediately.

The commentator begins by addressing a theological dispute: are Paradise and Hell created now or will they be created later? Drawing on the Jawharah's text, he affirms the majority view that they are already created, then clarifies two additional points: the certain fate of the Prophets' children and the inclusion of jinn in the same categories of happiness and wretchedness.

Guided Path
1
Locate the opening argument
Read the first sentence of the passage. It starts with 'Then [there is] the response to those who say...' What is the commentator responding to?
The denial of current creation of Paradise and Hell.
2
Identify the majority position
The commentator states 'Paradise is with the majority.' What does this mean? It means most scholars believe Paradise and Hell are created now.
This is a standard Ash'ari position.
3
Note the consensus on children of Prophets
The passage says 'as for the children of the Prophets, they are in Paradise by consensus.' Why is this important? It shows certainty about their salvation.
This is a point of certainty in Sunni theology.
4
Observe the inclusion of jinn
The passage extends the categories of happy and wretched to jinn. What does this imply? That jinn are morally responsible beings with eternal destinies.
Jinn are not mentioned in the original Jawharah verse here, but the commentator adds it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ففي الرَّدُ على القائلينَ بعدم خَلْق الجنَّة والنار الآن الجنة عند الجمهور، وأما أولاد الأنبياء ففي الجنة إجماعاً. ويدخل في السعيد والشقي من كان من الجن كذلك، وعلم من النظم أن عصاة المؤمنين لا يخلدون في النار إن دخلوها؛ لأنهم سعداء، فدار خلودهم الجنة، وفهم من دوام عذاب المخلدين أن غيرهم لا يدوم عذابه مدة بقائه، كعصاة الموحدين أهل الطبقة العليا، بل يموتون بعد الدخول لحظة ما، يعلم الله مقدارها فلا يحيون حتى يخرجوا منها؛ فداخل النار ما معذب فيها بنوع من أنواع عذابها، أو بأنواع متعددة منه مدة بقائه فيها، وداخل الجنة منعم فيها بنوع من أنواع نعيمها، أو بأنواع متعددة منه مدة إقامته بها بعد دخوله مهما بقي كل من الفريقين في إحدى الدارين.
Then [there is] the response to those who say that Paradise and Hell are not created now: Paradise is with the majority [of scholars], and as for the children of the Prophets, they are in Paradise by consensus. And enters into the happy and the wretched whoever is among the jinn likewise. And it is understood from the [poetic] composition that the disobedient believers are not eternally punished in Hell if they enter it; because they are happy, so their abode of eternity is Paradise. And it is understood from the perpetual punishment of the eternally [punished] that others do not have their punishment last the duration of their stay, like the disobedient monotheists, the people of the highest rank; rather they die after entering for a moment, whose measure God knows, and they do not live until they are brought out of it. So the inhabitant of Hell is punished therein with a type of its punishment, or with multiple types thereof, for the duration of his stay therein; and the inhabitant of Paradise is blessed therein with a type of its bliss, or with multiple types thereof, for the duration of his residence therein after his entrance, as long as each of the two groups remains in one of the two abodes.
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation and refutation. It begins by stating the position of the majority (جمهور) that Paradise and Hell are already created now, in response to those who deny this. It then clarifies that the children of the Prophets are in Paradise by consensus. Next, it explains that the category of 'happy' and 'wretched' includes the jinn as well. From the poetic text (النظم) of the Jawharah, it is understood that disobedient believers (عصاة المؤمنين) are not eternally punished in Hell if they enter it; because they are ultimately 'happy' (سعداء), their eternal abode is Paradise. Furthermore, from the everlasting punishment of those destined to be eternally damned, it is understood that others—specifically disobedient monotheists (عصاة الموحدين) of the highest rank (الطبقة العليا)—do not have their punishment last for the entire duration of their stay. Instead, they die after entering Hell for a brief moment known only to God, and remain lifeless until they are taken out. The passage then defines the condition of inhabitants: the inhabitant of Hell is punished with some type(s) of punishment for his stay, and the inhabitant of Paradise is blessed with some type(s) of bliss for his stay, for as long as each group remains in its respective abode.

Key Terms
الجنَّة
النار
السعيد
الشقي
الجن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the status of the children of the Prophets?
A) They are in a waiting place until judgment.
B) They are in Paradise by consensus.
C) They are judged individually based on deeds.
D) They are not included in the categories of happy or wretched.

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are created now; children of Prophets and righteous jinn enter Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Paradise and Hell are already created and real now, what does that mean for how you view your daily choices? Do you live with the awareness that the fire is already burning and the garden is already waiting?
?
The Prophet's children are in Paradise by consensus. How does this certainty about the fate of those who could not choose affect your hope and prayer for the children you know who have passed away?
?
The jinn are also judged as happy or wretched. Have you ever considered the reality of the jinn and their accountability? How should this enlarge your understanding of God's justice and mercy?

The Fate of Disobedient Believers in Hell
Explains temporary punishment of sinful believers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that sinful believers (عصاة المؤمنين) who enter Hell do not remain there eternally; instead, they die for a brief moment known only to Allah and are then brought out to Paradise.

Core Idea
Sinful believers die temporarily in Hell, then enter Paradise eternally.

The commentator now explains a critical point derived from the Jawharah's poem: what happens to believers who commit major sins and enter Hell? Based on the text, he shows that such believers are ultimately 'happy' (سعداء) and therefore their eternal home is Paradise. From the everlasting punishment of the damned, we learn that others—specifically sinful monotheists—are not punished throughout their stay but die momentarily.

Guided Path
1
Find the key deduction
Read the sentence starting with 'وعلم من النظم'. What is the source of knowledge? The 'نظم' (poetic composition) of the Jawharah.
This shows the commentator is interpreting the poem.
2
Understand why they are not eternally punished
The passage says they are not eternally punished 'لأنهم سعداء' (because they are happy). What does 'happy' mean here? It means they are ultimately destined for Paradise.
Their core identity as believers overrides their sins.
3
Grasp the mechanism
The passage says they 'يموتون بعد الدخول لحظة ما' (they die after entering for a moment). What does this imply? Their punishment is not continuous; they are taken out of Hell after dying.
This is a specific Ash'ari view on temporary punishment.
4
Connect to the eternally damned
The passage contrasts them with 'المخلدين' (the eternally [punished]). What does this contrast teach? It clarifies that the duration of punishment differs for different groups.
The eternally damned remain forever in Hell.

The Condition of Inhabitants in Paradise and Hell
Defines the experience of dwellers in both abodes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the general definition of what it means to be an inhabitant of Paradise or Hell: each dweller experiences either one or multiple types of bliss or punishment for the duration of their stay.

Core Idea
Inhabitants experience their abode's bliss or punishment in various types throughout their stay.

After explaining the fate of different groups, the commentator provides a formal definition of what it means to be a 'داخل النار' (inhabitant of Hell) or 'داخل الجنة' (inhabitant of Paradise). He describes their experience in terms of types of punishment or bliss and the duration of their stay. This definition applies to all inhabitants, whether eternal or temporary.

Guided Path
1
Read the final sentence
Focus on the last part starting with 'فداخل النار'. This is a definition. What two categories does it mention?
Hell inhabitant and Paradise inhabitant.
2
Identify the components of the definition
For each inhabitant, the definition includes: the type of experience (punishment or bliss), multiplicity (one or many types), and duration (the stay).
This is a precise theological definition.
3
Note the emphasis on duration
The phrase 'مدة بقائه فيها' (duration of his stay therein) appears for both. Why is duration important? Because it acknowledges that stays can be temporary or permanent.
This applies to both eternal and temporary dwellers.
4
Reflect on the balance
The definition treats both abodes symmetrically. What does this imply about the justice of Allah? Each person receives exactly the experience appropriate to their stay.
No one will be treated unfairly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ففي الرَّدُ على القائلينَ بعدم خَلْق الجنَّة والنار الآن الجنة عند الجمهور، وأما أولاد الأنبياء ففي الجنة إجماعاً. ويدخل في السعيد والشقي من كان من الجن كذلك، وعلم من النظم أن عصاة المؤمنين لا يخلدون في النار إن دخلوها؛ لأنهم سعداء، فدار خلودهم الجنة، وفهم من دوام عذاب المخلدين أن غيرهم لا يدوم عذابه مدة بقائه، كعصاة الموحدين أهل الطبقة العليا، بل يموتون بعد الدخول لحظة ما، يعلم الله مقدارها فلا يحيون حتى يخرجوا منها؛ فداخل النار ما معذب فيها بنوع من أنواع عذابها، أو بأنواع متعددة منه مدة بقائه فيها، وداخل الجنة منعم فيها بنوع من أنواع نعيمها، أو بأنواع متعددة منه مدة إقامته بها بعد دخوله مهما بقي كل من الفريقين في إحدى الدارين.
Then [there is] the response to those who say that Paradise and Hell are not created now: Paradise is with the majority [of scholars], and as for the children of the Prophets, they are in Paradise by consensus. And enters into the happy and the wretched whoever is among the jinn likewise. And it is understood from the [poetic] composition that the disobedient believers are not eternally punished in Hell if they enter it; because they are happy, so their abode of eternity is Paradise. And it is understood from the perpetual punishment of the eternally [punished] that others do not have their punishment last the duration of their stay, like the disobedient monotheists, the people of the highest rank; rather they die after entering for a moment, whose measure God knows, and they do not live until they are brought out of it. So the inhabitant of Hell is punished therein with a type of its punishment, or with multiple types thereof, for the duration of his stay therein; and the inhabitant of Paradise is blessed therein with a type of its bliss, or with multiple types thereof, for the duration of his residence therein after his entrance, as long as each of the two groups remains in one of the two abodes.
Source pages p. 550

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal explanation and refutation. It begins by stating the position of the majority (جمهور) that Paradise and Hell are already created now, in response to those who deny this. It then clarifies that the children of the Prophets are in Paradise by consensus. Next, it explains that the category of 'happy' and 'wretched' includes the jinn as well. From the poetic text (النظم) of the Jawharah, it is understood that disobedient believers (عصاة المؤمنين) are not eternally punished in Hell if they enter it; because they are ultimately 'happy' (سعداء), their eternal abode is Paradise. Furthermore, from the everlasting punishment of those destined to be eternally damned, it is understood that others—specifically disobedient monotheists (عصاة الموحدين) of the highest rank (الطبقة العليا)—do not have their punishment last for the entire duration of their stay. Instead, they die after entering Hell for a brief moment known only to God, and remain lifeless until they are taken out. The passage then defines the condition of inhabitants: the inhabitant of Hell is punished with some type(s) of punishment for his stay, and the inhabitant of Paradise is blessed with some type(s) of bliss for his stay, for as long as each group remains in its respective abode.

The Obligation to Believe in the Prophet's Hawd
Commentator refutes Mu'tazila denial of Hawd and explains its obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the Hawd (basin) of the Prophet ﷺ is obligatory, based on transmitted evidence, and that denying it is a serious sin.

Core Idea
Denying the Hawd makes one an innovator and sinner; belief is obligatory.

The Mu'tazila denied the Hawd, a physical basin granted to the Prophet in the afterlife. The commentator here affirms its reality and the obligation to believe in it, warning that denial leads to being labeled an innovator and sinner. This lesson unpacks the passage that establishes this doctrine from transmitted sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the key terms: الحوض, حتم, مبتدع, فاسق.
The passage begins with a response to the Mu'tazila.
2
Identify the ruling and consequences
Find where the passage states that belief in the Hawd is 'حتم' (obligatory) and lists what happens to one who denies it. Note the terms 'مبتدع' and 'فاسق'.
3
Understand the nature of the Hawd
Read the physical description: a specific large body of water with wide sides, and the promise that those who drink never thirst again.
This shows the Hawd is a concrete reality, not metaphorical.
4
Recognize the basis of obligation
Note the phrase 'كما قد جاءنا في النقل' which indicates the obligation is based on transmitted evidence (Quran and hadith).
The source references the two Sahihs, emphasizing authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولمَّا نفت المعتزلةُ الحوض أشار إلى الرَّدِّ عليهم بوجوب الإيمان به، فقال (إيمَانُنَا) أي تصديقنا معاشرَ المُكلَّفين (بِحَوْضِ خَيْرِ الرُّسُلِ) أي: بالحوض الذي يُعطَاهُ في الآخرة أفضلُ المرسلين، وهو نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم (حَتْمٌ) أي واجبٌ؛ فيثاب عليه مَن صدَّق به، ويُبدع ويفسق جاحده، وهو: جسم مخصوص كبيرٌ مُتَّسِعُ الجوانب، تَرِدُه هذه الأمة، مَن شَرِبَ منه لا يَظمأ أبدًا. وأشار إلى أن وجوب الإيمان به سمعي بقوله: (كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَنَا) أي للنَّصِّ الذي ورد إلينا (فِي النَّقْل) ففي الصحيحين من حديث عبد الله بن
And when the Mu'tazila denied the Hawd, he alluded to refuting them by [stating] the obligation of believing in it, so he said: 'Our belief' — that is, our affirmation, O community of legally responsible persons — 'in the Hawd of the best of the Messengers' — that is, the Hawd that is given in the Hereafter to the best of the Messengers, and he is our Prophet Muhammad ﷺ — 'is obligatory' (حَتْمٌ), i.e., incumbent; so the one who affirms it is rewarded, and the one who denies it is considered an innovator and a sinner. And it is a specific large body, wide of sides, to which this nation will come; whoever drinks from it will never thirst forever. And he indicated that the obligation of believing in it is based on transmitted [evidence] by his saying: 'As has come to us' — i.e., [based on] the text that has reached us — 'in transmission (فِي النَّقْل); for in the two Sahihs from the hadith of Abdullah ibn...
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who denied the Hawd (basin) of the Prophet ﷺ. The commentator explains that the poet (in the original Jawharah) signaled the obligation to believe in the Hawd as a response to them. The phrase 'إيماننا بحوض خير الرسل حتم' is parsed: 'إيماننا' means our affirmation (تصديق) as accountable individuals; 'بحوض خير الرسل' refers to the specific basin granted to the Prophet in the afterlife; 'حتم' means obligatory (واجب). The commentator then describes the consequences: belief in it earns reward, while denial (جحود) leads to being labeled an innovator (مبتدع) and sinful (فاسق). A physical description follows: the Hawd is a specific large body of water (جسم مخصوص) with wide sides, which this nation (these الأمة) will come to; whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. Finally, the commentator emphasizes that the obligation to believe in it is derived from transmitted evidence (سمعي) by citing the phrase 'كما قد جاءنا في النقل', pointing to the textual proofs in the canonical hadith collections.

Obligation to Believe in the Prophet's Pool (Hawd)
Sanusi affirms the obligation to believe in the Hawd and provides hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in the Hawd is obligatory according to Sunni theology and the scriptural evidence supporting its reality.

Core Idea
Belief in the Hawd is obligatory based on authentic transmitted reports; denial is innovation and sin.

Sanusi moves from theological principles to practical beliefs in the unseen. The Hawd (Pool) of the Prophet ﷺ is a well-attested eschatological reality affirmed by authentic hadith. This passage establishes its doctrinal status and defends it against those who reject it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Let the author's words set the foundation.
Notice the strong language: 'obligatory' and 'innovator/sinner' for deniers.
2
Identify the ruling and consequence
Determine the ruling on belief in the Hawd and the consequence for denial according to the text.
The denier is declared an innovator (mubtadiʿ) and sinful (fāsiq), not a disbeliever.
3
Examine the hadith evidence and reconciliation
Look at the hadith from the two Sahihs and how the author reconciles apparent differences in reported dimensions.
The reconciliation shows the Prophet ﷺ gradually informed of greater size.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إيمانُنَا بِحَوضِ خَيْرِ الرُّسُلِ حَتْمٌ كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَنَا فِي النَّقْلِ
ولمَّا نفى المُعتزلةُ الحوض أشار إلى الرَّدِّ عليهم بوجوب الإيمان به، فقال (إيمَانُنَا) أي تصديقنا معاشرَ المُكلَّفين (بِحَوْضِ خَيْرِ الرُّسُلِ) أي: بالحوض الذي يُعطَاهُ في الآخرة أفضلُ المرسلين، وهو نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم (حَتْمٌ) أي واجب؛ فيثاب عليه مَن صدَّق به، ويُبدع ويفسق جاحده، وهو: جسم مخصوص كبيرٌ مُتَّسِعُ الجوانب، تَرِدُه هذه الأمة، مَن شَرِبَ منه لا يَظمأ أبدًا. وأشار إلى أن وجوب الإيمان به سمعي بقوله: (كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَنَا) أي للنَّصِّ الذي ورد إلينا (فِي النَّقْل) ففي الصَّحيحين من حديث عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص: حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيض من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكِيزَانُه أكثرُ مِن نجوم السَّماء، مَن شرب منه فلا يظمأ أبداً. وما ورد من تحديده بجهات مختلفة إما بحسب من حضره ممن يعرف تلك الجهة؛ فخاطب كل قوم بالجهة التي يعرفونها، أو أنه أخبر أولا بالمسافة اليسيرة، ثمَّ أُعلِمَ بالمسافة الطّويلة، فأخبر بها، كأنَّ الله سبحانه تفضّل عليه باتساعه شيئا فشيئا؛ فيكون الاعتماد على ما يدلُّ على أطولها مسافة، كما أشار إليه النووي رحمه الله تعالى. وفيما أَوْحَى الله إلى عيسى من صفة نبينا: اله حوض أبعد من مكّة إلى مطلع الشمس، فيه آنية مثل عدد نجوم السَّماء، وله لون كل شراب الجنَّة وطعم كل ثمار الجنَّة. وظواهر الأحاديث أنَّه بجانب الجنّة.
Our faith in the pool of the best of messengers is obligatory, just as it has come to us in transmission. When the Mu'tazila denied the pool, he indicated the refutation of them by the obligation of belief in it. He said ('Faith of us') i.e. our affirmation, we the legally responsible, ('in the pool of the best of the messengers') i.e. the pool which will be given in the Hereafter to the best of the messengers, and he is our Prophet Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace, ('obligatory') i.e. incumbent; so the one who affirms it is rewarded, and the one who denies it is declared an innovator and a sinner. And it is a specific large body, wide in sides, which this community will approach; whoever drinks from it will never thirst. And he indicated that the obligation of belief in it is based on revelation by his saying ('as has come to us') i.e. because of the text that has reached us ('in transmission'), for in the two Sahihs from the hadith of Abdullah bin Amr bin al-Aas: 'My pool is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its scent is better than musk, its drinking vessels are more numerous than the stars of the sky; whoever drinks from it will never thirst.' And what has come of its determination by different directions is either according to the one present who knows that direction, so he addressed each people by the direction they know, or that he first informed of the short distance, then was informed of the long distance, so he informed of it, as if God, exalted is He, favored him by its expansion little by little; so reliance is on what indicates the longest distance, as al-Nawawi, may God have mercy on him, indicated. And in what God revealed to Jesus of the description of our Prophet: 'He has a pool farther than Mecca to the rising of the sun, in it are vessels like the number of the stars of the sky, and it has the color of every drink of Paradise and the taste of every fruit of Paradise.' And the apparent meanings of the hadiths are that it is alongside Paradise.
Source pages p. 551

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the line of poetry affirming the obligation to believe in the Hawd (Pool) of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ. The author begins by explaining that the Mu'tazila denied the Hawd, so the poet refutes them by declaring belief in it obligatory. The author clarifies that 'our faith' means the affirmation by those who are legally responsible, and the 'best of messengers' is Muhammad ﷺ. The ruling is 'obligatory' (ḥatm), meaning incumbent: the believer who affirms it is rewarded, and the denier is considered an innovator and sinful. The Hawd is described as a specific large body with wide sides; the Muslim community will come to it, and whoever drinks once will never thirst again. The author then notes that the obligation is based on revelation (samʿī), as indicated by the phrase 'as has come to us in transmission'. The proof is the hadith in al-Bukhari and Muslim from ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿAmr ibn al-ʿĀṣ, describing the Hawd's size (a month's journey), its water (whiter than milk), its scent (better than musk), its vessels (more numerous than stars), and the promise that the drinker never thirsts. The author then addresses apparent contradictions in reports about the Hawd's dimensions and location. He offers two reconciliations: either the Prophet ﷺ addressed each group by a direction they recognized, or he was gradually informed of increasing size and reported the larger one. The preferred view is to rely on the longest distance, as mentioned by al-Nawawī. The author adds a report from earlier scriptures revealed to Jesus describing the Prophet's Hawd as being farther than Mecca to the sunrise, with vessels like stars and containing the colors and tastes of Paradise. Finally, he notes that the outward meaning of the hadiths places the Hawd alongside Paradise, implying its location near the entrance or after the bridge Ṣirāṭ.

Key Terms
