إيمان
حَتْم
سمعي
نقل
جاحِد

الفسق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hawd is a metaphorical symbol, not a real physical pool.
Correction: The text affirms it as a specific large body with clear dimensions and properties, and its denial is a blameworthy innovation.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway

Obligation to Believe in the Prophet's Basin
States the obligation to believe in the basin and discusses its description and location.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the Prophet's basin is obligatory, its described attributes, how to reconcile different reports about its size, and that not knowing its chronological order does not harm faith.

Core Idea
Belief in the basin is obligatory; its exact timing is not essential.

This passage from the Jawhara establishes the obligation to believe in the Prophet's basin (al-hawd), a heavenly fountain exclusive to the Prophet Muhammad. It presents a vivid hadith description, reconciles varying reports about its dimensions, and clarifies that only belief in its existence is required — not knowledge of its sequence relative to other eschatological events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with the obligation statement.
2
Identify the obligation and description
The passage states that belief in the basin is obligatory. Then it quotes a hadith describing its size, water, smell, vessels, and the effect of drinking from it.
The hadith from 'Amr ibn al-'As emphasizes the vastness and qualities of the basin.
3
Understand the reconciliation
Follow how the passage harmonizes different narrations about the basin's dimensions—either tailored to audiences or gradual revelation. Finally, note the ruling that ignorance of its chronological order relative to the Sirat does not harm belief.
The reconciliation highlights that reliance is on the longest distance, as per al-Nawawi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجوب الإيمان بحوض سيد الأنبياء. عمرو بن العاص: حوضي مسيرة شهر وزواياه سواء، ماؤه أبيض من اللبن، وريحه أطيب من المسك، وكيزانه أكثر من نجوم السماء، من شرب منه فلا يظمأ أبداً. وما ورد من تحديده بجهات مختلفة إما بحسب من حضره ممن يعرف تلك الجهة؛ فخاطب كل قوم بالجهة التي يعرفونها، أو أنه أخبر أولا بالمسافة اليسيرة، ثم أُعلِمَ بالمسافة الطويلة، فأخبر بها، كأن الله سبحانه تفضل عليه باتساعه شيئا فشيئا؛ فيكون الاعتماد على ما يدل على أطولها مسافة، كما أشار إليه النووي رحمه الله تعالى، وفيما أوحى الله إلى عيسى من صفة نبينا: له حوض أبعد من مكة إلى مطلع الشمس، فيه آنية مثل عدد نجوم السماء، وله لون كل شراب الجنة وطعم كل ثمار الجنة. وظواهر الأحاديث أنه بجانب الجنة كما قاله ابن حجر، والواجب اعتقاد ثبوته، وجهل تقدمه على الصراط أو تأخره لا يضر بالاعتقاد.
Obligation of belief in the basin of the master of prophets. 'Amr ibn al-'As: My basin is a month's journey, its corners are equal, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is more fragrant than musk, and its vessels are more numerous than the stars of the sky; whoever drinks from it will never thirst again. And what has been reported of defining it with different directions—either according to those present who know that direction, so he addressed each people by the direction they know, or that he first informed of the short distance, then was informed of the long distance, so he informed of it, as if Allah the Exalted favored him by its expansion little by little; so reliance is upon what indicates its longest distance, as indicated by al-Nawawi, may Allah have mercy on him. And in what Allah revealed to Jesus describing our Prophet: he has a basin farther than Mecca to the rising of the sun, containing vessels like the number of the stars of the sky, and having the color of every drink of Paradise and the taste of every fruit of Paradise. And the apparent meanings of the hadiths are that it is beside Paradise, as Ibn Hajar said. And it is obligatory to believe in its existence, and ignorance of its precedence over the Sirat or its delay does not harm belief.
Source pages p. 552

Commentary
This passage defines the obligation to believe in the Prophet's basin (al-hawd). It begins by stating that belief in it is obligatory. Then it cites a hadith from 'Amr ibn al-'As describing the basin's size, water, smell, vessels, and the effect of drinking from it. Next, it addresses the different narrations about the basin's dimensions and locations, reconciling them by suggesting the Prophet tailored descriptions to his audience or received progressive revelations. The author concludes that the correct distance is the longest, as per al-Nawawi. A further revelation to Jesus is mentioned, emphasizing the basin's vastness. The apparent meaning of hadiths places the basin beside Paradise, but the author clarifies that only belief in its existence is obligatory; not knowing whether it comes before or after the Sirat does not harm one's faith.

Key Terms
الحوض
الصراط
الميزان
السمعيات
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That one must know the exact chronological order of eschatological events, specifically whether the basin comes before or after the Sirat.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that ignorance of this order does not harm belief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding knowledge of whether the basin comes before or after the Sirat?
A) It is obligatory to know.
B) Ignorance of it does not harm belief.
C) It is a severe sin to be ignorant.
D) It is a matter of ijtihad.

Key Takeaway
It is obligatory to believe in the Prophet's basin, but one's faith is not harmed by not knowing whether it precedes or follows the Sirat.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly long to drink from the Prophet's basin? What in your life right now might prevent you from being among those who drink from it? What will you change today to increase your hope and preparation?
?
If the basin's exact timing is not required for belief, why do you sometimes get caught up in arguing about details of the afterlife instead of focusing on the state of your own heart and actions? Will you commit to prioritizing inner purification over theological debate?
?
The basin's water is described as pure, fragrant, and thirst-quenching. Is your heart as pure and your deeds as fragrant in the sight of Allah? If the Prophet were to see your life today, would he be pleased to welcome you to his basin? What one step will you take this week to purify your intentions?

Who Drinks from the Basin and Who Is Repelled
Explains verse 112 on the basin, covenant, and tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the explanation of verse 112 regarding the Prophet's basin, including who will drink from it and who will be repelled, and the basis for belief in these reports.

Core Idea
The basin is for covenant-keepers; transgressors are repelled.

This passage unpacks the meaning of a line from the poem that describes the events at the Prophet's basin on the Day of Judgment. It clarifies who will be allowed to drink and who will be prevented, grounding the discussion in the hadith corpus that reports these events.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and explanation
Begin by reading the verse in Arabic and its literal translation. Notice the structure: it is part of the Sam'iyyat (matters of the unseen).
2
Understand the covenant
The 'covenant' (al-ʿahd) refers to the primordial pact taken from all souls. Those who fulfill it die in faith without changing or altering.
The passage notes this description could include previous nations, but hadith limit the basin to this Ummah.
3
Distinguish the Prophet's basin
Why is our Prophet's basin specially mentioned? Because its reports are mutawatir (mass-transmitted), while others are ahad (single-chain). This is a key point about how we know such matters.
4
Identify the repelled
Those repelled are people who changed and altered the covenant, i.e., abandoned Islam after it reached them. Allah accepts no other religion from such a person.
5
Recognize the obligation
The passage concludes that belief in these reports is obligatory because they reach the level of moral tawatur (overwhelming certainty).

Source Text

قسم السمعيات
عنه بِعَهْدِهِمْ وَقُلْ يُذَادُ مَنْ طَغَوا ١١٢ - يَنَالُ شُرْبًا مِنْهُ أَقْوَامٌ وَفَوا
( يَنَالُ شُرْبًا مِنْهُ) أي: يتعاطى الشرب من ذلك الحوض لدفع العطش، أو للتلذذ، أو لتعجيل المسرة (أَقْوَامٌ وَفَوْا) الله تعالى (بِعَهْدِهِمْ) وهو الميثاق الذي أخذه الله عليهم في الإيمان به، وباليوم الآخر، واتباع دينه وشرائعه، وتصديق كتبه ورسله، حين أخرجهم من ظهر آدم، وأشهدهم على أنفسهم، فماتوا على ذلك لم يغيروا ولم يبدلوا، وهذا الوصف وإن شمل الأمم السابقة لكنه خلاف ظواهر الأحاديث أنه لا يرده إلا مؤمنو جميع مؤمني هذه الأمة؛ لأن كل أمة إنما ترد حوض نبيها (1)، وتخصيص حوض نبينا بالذكر لوروده بالأحاديث البالغة مبلغ التواتر، بخلاف غيره لوروده بالآحاد. (وَقُلْ يُذَادُ) أي: يطرد عنه، فلا يشرب منه (مَنْ طَغَوْا) أي: أقوام غيروا وبدلوا عهدهم الذي أخذه الله عليهم، وهو الإسلام الذي ألزمهم اتباعه، ولم يقبل ممن بلغه دينا غيره (2)، كما وردت بذلك الآثار الصحيحة والحسنة البالغ مجموعها مبلغ التواتر المعنوي، وكل ما هو كذلك فالإيمان به واجب.
(1) قوله: (إنما ترد حوض نبيها) لما ورد عن الحسن مرفوعا: «إن لكل نبيا حوضا، وهو قائم على حوضه وبيده عصا يدعو من عرف من أمته، ألا وإنهم يتباهون أيهم أكثر تبعا، وإني لأرجو أن أكون أكثرهم تبعا» الشنواني. والحديث عند الترمذي بلفظ قريب.
(2) قوله: (ولم يقبل ممن بلغه دينا غيره) عطف على قوله: (ألزمهم اتباعه) أي: ولم يقبل الله من شخص بلغه دين الإسلام دينا غيره الشنواني.
Section of the Sam'iyyat. From it: with their covenant, and say: those who transgress are repelled. 112 - They obtain a drink from it, a people who fulfilled. (They obtain a drink from it) means: they take the drink from that basin to repel thirst, or for pleasure, or to hasten joy. (A people who fulfilled) Allah Almighty (their covenant) which is the covenant that Allah took from them to believe in Him, the Last Day, and to follow His religion and laws, and to believe in His books and messengers, when He brought them out from the back of Adam and made them testify against themselves, and they died upon that without changing or altering. This description, although it includes previous nations, contradicts the apparent meanings of the hadiths that none come to it except all believers of this nation; because every nation only comes to the basin of its own prophet (1), and the specification of our Prophet's basin by mention is because it is reported through hadiths that reach the level of tawatur, unlike others which are reported through ahad. (And say: those who transgress are repelled) means: they are driven away from it, so they do not drink from it (those who transgress) meaning: people who changed and altered their covenant which Allah took from them, which is Islam that He obligated them to follow, and He does not accept from one who has received it any other religion (2), as has been reported through authentic and good narrations whose total reaches the level of moral tawatur, and everything that is so, belief in it is obligatory. (1) His statement: (Only comes to the basin of its prophet) because of what has been reported from al-Hasan raised: 'Indeed every prophet has a basin, and he stands at his basin with a staff in his hand calling those he knows from his nation, and indeed they boast about who has more followers, and I hope to be the one with the most followers' - al-Shanwani. The hadith is in al-Tirmidhi with a similar wording. (2) His statement: (And He does not accept from one who has received it any other religion) is conjoined to his statement: (He obligated them to follow it) meaning: and Allah does not accept from a person who has received the religion of Islam any other religion - al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage explains verse 112 of the poem. It is part of the section on Sam'iyyat (matters known through revelation). The verse says: 'They obtain a drink from it, a people who fulfilled their covenant, and say: those who transgress are repelled.' The commentary proceeds in order: first, 'they obtain a drink from it' is explained as taking the drink to quench thirst, seek pleasure, or hasten joy. Second, 'a people who fulfilled their covenant with Allah' refers to the primordial covenant (mithaq) that Allah took from all souls when they were created from the loins of Adam, testifying to faith and obedience. They died faithful without change. Although this description could include previous nations, the apparent meaning of hadiths is that only the believers of this Ummah will come to this particular basin, because each nation goes to its own prophet's basin. The basin of our Prophet is singled out because its reports are mutawatir, while reports of other basins are ahad. Third, 'and say: those who transgress are repelled' means they are driven away and prevented from drinking. They are those who changed and altered their covenant, meaning they abandoned Islam. Allah does not accept any other religion from someone who has received Islam. The passage concludes that such reports, even if not individually mutawatir, are collectively mutawatir in meaning, and belief in them is obligatory. Two footnotes elaborate: one quotes a hadith that every prophet has a basin; the other clarifies that Allah does not accept any religion other than Islam from those who have received it.

Key Terms
الحوض
العهد
الطغيان
التواتر
الآحاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the verse applies to all nations equally.
Correction: The commentary specifies that the primary referent is this Ummah due to the abundance of evidence (tawatur) regarding the Prophet's basin.

Checkpoint
Who are the people who will be repelled from the basin according to the passage?
A) Those who have not fulfilled their covenant.
B) Those who have changed and altered their covenant.
C) All non-Muslims.
D) Only the sinners of the Muslim community.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's basin is reserved for those who keep the covenant of faith, while transgressors who alter it are denied.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the covenant Allah made with you before you were born, how have you fulfilled it today in your choices? What one specific action can you take this week to live by that covenant more sincerely?
?
If you were to stand before the Prophet's basin tomorrow, would you be among those who drink or among those who are repelled? What evidence from your daily life supports your answer?
?
You have heard that the hadith about the basin are mutawatir—certain and true. Do you truly believe in the basin with certainty, or is it just a distant concept? What would change in your life if you really lived as if you might be denied that drink?

The Prophet's Basin and the Faithful
Explanation of the basin verse and the covenant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the Prophet's basin, the covenant of faith, and why faith in the basin is obligatory based on mutawatir hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet's basin is a reward for those who keep their covenant of faith.

In this lesson, we explore the first part of the commentary on verse 112, which describes the Prophet's basin and the believers who drink from it. The commentator explains the covenant taken from all humanity and emphasizes that only the faithful of this ummah will drink from our Prophet's basin, as confirmed by abundant hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation to grasp the commentator's explanation.
The passage includes footnotes that clarify points.
2
Identify the covenant and its significance
The covenant is the primordial pledge to believe in Allah, the Last Day, and follow His messengers. Those who die keeping it are faithful.
3
Understand why the basin is specific to this ummah
The commentator notes that each prophet has a basin, but our Prophet's basin is singled out because it is confirmed by mutawatir hadiths.
This counters a potential misunderstanding.
4
Recognize the role of mutawatir hadith
Belief in the basin is obligatory because the narrations reach the level of tawatur. This is a key principle in kalam.

(1) قوله : (إنما ترد حوض نبيها لما ورد عن الحسن مرفوعا: «إنَّ لكل حوضا، وهو قائم على حوضه وبيده عصا يدعو من عرف من أمته، ألا وإنهم يتباهون أيهم أكثر تبعا، وإني لأرجو أن أكون أكثرهم تبعا الشنواني والحديث عند الترمذي بلفظ قريب.

Section of the heard matters. Ibn Hajar, and it is obligatory to believe in its affirmation, and ignorance of its precedence over the Bridge or its delay does not harm belief. From him. With their covenant, and say: He is driven away, whoever transgressed – 112 – A people obtain drink from it who were faithful. '(Obtain drink from it)' means: they engage in drinking from that basin to quench thirst, or for pleasure, or to hasten joy. '(A people who were faithful)' to Allah Almighty '(with their covenant)' which is the covenant that Allah took from them in faith in Him, and in the Last Day, and following His religion and laws, and believing in His books and messengers, when He brought them out from the loins of Adam and made them testify over [?], and they died upon that, not changing nor altering. And this description, even if it includes previous nations, contradicts the apparent meanings of hadiths that only the believers of themselves, all believers of this ummah, will come to it; because every nation only comes to the basin of its prophet (1), and singling out our Prophet's basin for mention is due to its being reported in hadiths reaching the level of tawatur, unlike others which are reported in ahad. '(And say: He is driven away)' meaning: he is repelled from it, so he does not drink from it. '(Whoever transgressed)' meaning: people who changed and altered their covenant which Allah took from them, which is Islam that He obligated them to follow, and He does not accept from anyone to whom it has reached any religion other than it (2), as the authentic and good narrations have come, the sum of which reaches the level of tawatur. And everything that is like that, having faith in it is obligatory. (1) His statement: 'Every nation only comes to the basin of its prophet' based on what is reported from al-Hasan marfu'an: 'Indeed, for every prophet is a basin, and he stands at his basin with a staff in his hand, calling those he recognizes from his ummah. Indeed, they boast about which has more followers, and I hope to have the most followers.' – al-Shanwani, and the hadith is with al-Tirmidhi with a similar wording. (2) His statement: 'And He does not accept from anyone to whom it has reached any religion other than it' is a conjunction to his statement: 'He obligated them to follow it,' meaning: Allah does not accept from a person to whom the religion of Islam has reached any religion other than it – al-Shanwani. So the apostate is among the driven away, and whoever innovates in the religion what Allah does not approve, and whoever opposes the community of Muslims, like the Kharijites, the Rawafid, and the Mu'tazila with their different sects, because they are changers, rather they are more severely repelled than others, and the oppressive tyrants, and the one who openly commits major sins, the one who treats minor sins lightly, and the people of deviation and innovation. But the one who changes through apostasy is eternally in the Fire, and the one who changes through sins is under the will (1), and Allah knows best. (1) His statement: 'under the will' meaning: the will of Allah; if He wills He pardons him, and if He wills He punishes him, and among the punishment is not drinking from the basin – al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on verse 112 of the poem, dealing with the prophetic basin (al-hawd). The commentator begins by stating the section on the heard matters and notes the obligation to believe in the basin's existence. He then explains the verse: 'A people obtain drink from it who were faithful with their covenant.' The covenant is the one taken from all humanity in pre-eternity, and those who uphold it are the believers of this ummah. The commentator clarifies that although the description could apply to previous nations, hadiths indicate that only the believers of the Prophet Muhammad will drink from his basin. This is because each prophet has his own basin, but our Prophet's basin is specifically mentioned due to the abundant mutawatir hadiths. Then the phrase 'say: He is driven away, whoever transgressed' is explained: those who are repelled are those who changed and altered the covenant of Islam. The commentator lists categories of such people: apostates, innovators (like Kharijites, Rawafid, Mu'tazila), oppressive rulers, open sinners, and those of deviation. A distinction is made: the apostate is eternally punished, while the sinner is under God's will, possibly pardoned or punished.

Key Terms
الحوض
العهد
الوفاء
التواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's basin is for all believers of every prophet, not just Muhammad's ummah.
Correction: The passage clarifies that each prophet has a basin for his own followers, and our Prophet's basin is specifically for his ummah, as established by mutawatir hadiths.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes the basin of the Prophet Muhammad from the basins of other prophets?
A) It is larger and more splendid.
B) It is reported in mutawatir hadiths, while others are in ahad hadiths.
C) Only the Prophet Muhammad intercedes for his ummah at his basin.
D) It is mentioned in the Quran explicitly.

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Prophet's basin is obligatory because it is established by mutawatir hadith, and it is reserved for those who keep the covenant of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have made a covenant with Allah—are you keeping it? Look at your life today: which moments show you are 'wafaw' (faithful) and which reveal 'taghaw' (transgression)? What would it mean to stand at the Prophet's basin and be driven away?
?
The lesson says ignorance of the basin's timing does not harm belief. But your actions are not ignorant—you know the covenant. Are you living as if you will drink, or as if you will be pushed back? What needs to change tonight?
?
The Prophet's basin is for those who did not change their covenant. Have you changed yours? When did you last renew your commitment to Islam with sincerity? If the basin were presented to you now, would you be among those who drink or those who are driven away?

The Driven Away: Apostates, Innovators, and Sinners
Classification of those driven away from the basin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the categories of people who are driven away from the Prophet's basin and the distinction between apostasy and sin in terms of punishment.

Core Idea
Those who break the covenant are driven away, but the punishment differs between apostates and sinners.

In this lesson, we continue the commentary and learn about those who will be repelled from the basin. The commentator lists apostates, innovators, oppressors, and open sinners, and clarifies that apostates face eternal punishment while sinners are under God's will.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the list of categories and the final distinction.
The passage ends with a note about the will of Allah.
2
List the categories of the driven away
From the passage, identify each group mentioned: apostates, innovators (Kharijites, Rawafid, Mu'tazila), oppressive rulers, open sinners, and people of deviation.
Note that innovators are described as 'more severely repelled'.
3
Understand the distinction in punishment
The commentator distinguishes between those who change through apostasy and those who change through sins. Apostates are eternally punished, while sinners are under Allah's will.
This shows that not all driven away are equal in punishment.

Section of the heard matters. Ibn Hajar, and it is obligatory to believe in its affirmation, and ignorance of its precedence over the Bridge or its delay does not harm belief. From him. With their covenant, and say: He is driven away, whoever transgressed – 112 – A people obtain drink from it who were faithful. '(Obtain drink from it)' means: they engage in drinking from that basin to quench thirst, or for pleasure, or to hasten joy. '(A people who were faithful)' to Allah Almighty '(with their covenant)' which is the covenant that Allah took from them in faith in Him, and in the Last Day, and following His religion and laws, and believing in His books and messengers, when He brought them out from the loins of Adam and made them testify over [?], and they died upon that, not changing nor altering. And this description, even if it includes previous nations, contradicts the apparent meanings of hadiths that only the believers of themselves, all believers of this ummah, will come to it; because every nation only comes to the basin of its prophet (1), and singling out our Prophet's basin for mention is due to its being reported in hadiths reaching the level of tawatur, unlike others which are reported in ahad. '(And say: He is driven away)' meaning: he is repelled from it, so he does not drink from it. '(Whoever transgressed)' meaning: people who changed and altered their covenant which Allah took from them, which is Islam that He obligated them to follow, and He does not accept from anyone to whom it has reached any religion other than it (2), as the authentic and good narrations have come, the sum of which reaches the level of tawatur. And everything that is like that, having faith in it is obligatory. (1) His statement: 'Every nation only comes to the basin of its prophet' based on what is reported from al-Hasan marfu'an: 'Indeed, for every prophet is a basin, and he stands at his basin with a staff in his hand, calling those he recognizes from his ummah. Indeed, they boast about which has more followers, and I hope to have the most followers.' – al-Shanwani, and the hadith is with al-Tirmidhi with a similar wording. (2) His statement: 'And He does not accept from anyone to whom it has reached any religion other than it' is a conjunction to his statement: 'He obligated them to follow it,' meaning: Allah does not accept from a person to whom the religion of Islam has reached any religion other than it – al-Shanwani. So the apostate is among the driven away, and whoever innovates in the religion what Allah does not approve, and whoever opposes the community of Muslims, like the Kharijites, the Rawafid, and the Mu'tazila with their different sects, because they are changers, rather they are more severely repelled than others, and the oppressive tyrants, and the one who openly commits major sins, the one who treats minor sins lightly, and the people of deviation and innovation. But the one who changes through apostasy is eternally in the Fire, and the one who changes through sins is under the will (1), and Allah knows best. (1) His statement: 'under the will' meaning: the will of Allah; if He wills He pardons him, and if He wills He punishes him, and among the punishment is not drinking from the basin – al-Shanwani.
Source pages p. 553

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on verse 112 of the poem, dealing with the prophetic basin (al-hawd). The commentator begins by stating the section on the heard matters and notes the obligation to believe in the basin's existence. He then explains the verse: 'A people obtain drink from it who were faithful with their covenant.' The covenant is the one taken from all humanity in pre-eternity, and those who uphold it are the believers of this ummah. The commentator clarifies that although the description could apply to previous nations, hadiths indicate that only the believers of the Prophet Muhammad will drink from his basin. This is because each prophet has his own basin, but our Prophet's basin is specifically mentioned due to the abundant mutawatir hadiths. Then the phrase 'say: He is driven away, whoever transgressed' is explained: those who are repelled are those who changed and altered the covenant of Islam. The commentator lists categories of such people: apostates, innovators (like Kharijites, Rawafid, Mu'tazila), oppressive rulers, open sinners, and those of deviation. A distinction is made: the apostate is eternally punished, while the sinner is under God's will, possibly pardoned or punished.

المبتدع
المشيئة
الطغيان

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All driven away from the basin are treated equally, all eternally punished.
Correction: The passage differentiates between apostates (eternal punishment) and sinners (under Allah's will, possibly pardoned or punished).

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The driven away include apostates, innovators, oppressors, and open sinners, but only apostates are eternally punished; other sinners are under God's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Think about the minor sins you commit frequently—do you treat them as insignificant? How does this lesson's warning about those who 'treat minor sins lightly' challenge your daily choices?
?
Are you more concerned with being correct in your opinions or with being part of the Muslim community, even when it means accepting those you disagree with? What would the Prophet's basin reveal about your attachment to the community?

The Major Intercession of Prophet Muhammad: Obligatory Belief and Definition
Definition of intercession and explanation of three obligatory beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that accepting the major intercession of Prophet Muhammad is an obligatory belief based on revelation (samiyyat), its linguistic and technical definition, and the three underlying obligations implied in the passage.

Core Idea
Intercession is not a rational necessity but a revealed obligation.

This lesson explores a fundamental article of faith in Sunni Islam: the major intercession of the Prophet Muhammad. The passage establishes that belief in this intercession is obligatory by revelation (samiyyat), not by reason, and defines intercession in both linguistic and technical senses. Additionally, the text hints at three essential obligations that must be affirmed regarding intercession.

Guided Path
1
Understand the source of obligation
The passage declares intercession as 'obligatory by hearing' meaning it is a revealed truth, not a rational necessity. Recognize that this is a sam'iyyat matter.
The term 'sami'an' indicates reliance on revelation.
2
Define key terms
Learn the linguistic meaning of shafa'ah as 'al-waseelah wa at-talab' (the means and the request) and the technical definition as 'asking for good for others.' Also distinguish between 'mushaffa'' (with fatha) meaning the one whose intercession is accepted, and the variant with kasra meaning the one who accepts intercession.
This distinction clarifies who is interceding and who is accepting.
3
Identify the three implied obligations
The commentator indicates that the verse points to three obligatory beliefs: that intercession is true, that it is specifically for the Prophet Muhammad, and that it is a grant from Allah not prevented by any condition.
These obligations are implicit in the phrase 'mushaffa' Muhammad' and the context.

ثم شرع في نوع آخرَ مِن السَّمعيَّات وردت به(2) الآثار ، وانعقد عليه الإجماع قبل ظهور المُبتدعة ، فقال : (وَوَاجِبٌ) سمعا (3) عندنا أهل الحقِّ (شَفَاعَةُ المُشَفّع) بفتح الفاء: الَّذي تُقبل شفاعته(؟)، ورفع إبهامه بإبدال منه .

(1) قوله: (في المشيئة) أي : إرادة الله ؛ فإن شاء عفا عنه وإن شاء عاقبه ، ومن جملة العقاب عدم الشرب من الحوض. الشنواني .

Faith in the major intercession of our Prophet. 11 – And obligatory is the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted, Muhammad, presented, not prevented. Then he began another type of heard matters reported in the narrations, and consensus was established upon it before the appearance of the innovators. Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of the major intercession of the Prophet Muhammad. It begins by citing the verse: 'And obligatory is the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted, Muhammad, presented, not prevented.' The commentator notes that this is part of the heard matters (samiyyat) established by narrations and consensus before the innovators appeared. The verse declares intercession to be obligatory (by hearing, not reason) for the people of truth. The term 'al-mushaffa' (with fath on the fa) means the one whose intercession is accepted. The commentator then defines intercession: linguistically it means 'the means and the request'; technically it is 'asking for good for others.' Finally, the commentator indicates that the verse points to three obligatory beliefs that must be affirmed. The footnotes clarify that 'obligatory by hearing' means it is rationally possible, and that 'mushaffa' with kasr on the fa means the one who accepts intercession (not the intercessor).

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Prophet's major intercession is an obligatory revealed doctrine, and intercession is the act of asking for good for others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you believe in the Prophet's intercession, but have you ever seriously questioned whether your belief is merely intellectual submission or genuine heartfelt acceptance? If it is obligatory by revelation, not by reason, are you willing to submit even if you don't fully understand it? What would change in your life if you truly lived as though all your hope rested on that intercession?
?
The lesson defines intercession as 'asking for good for others.' The Prophet will intercede for his ummah. How does this challenge your own daily priorities? When was the last time you sincerely asked Allah for good for someone else without expecting anything in return? Can you name one person you will intercede for through du'a tonight?
?
Belief in intercession is a revealed obligation (سمعياً). Are you comfortable with the fact that your salvation may depend on matters you did not arrive at through your own logic? Does this humble you or make you uneasy? Take a moment to thank Allah for granting belief in this gift through revelation.

Categories of Those Denied the Prophet's Intercession
Lists categories of those denied intercession and their eternal fate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific categories of people who are denied the Prophet's intercession and their eternal fate according to this classical text.

Core Idea
Intercession is denied to apostates, innovators, oppressors, and open sinners who scorn disobedience.

This passage from Ithaaf al-Mureed classifies the types of people who are excluded from the Prophet's intercession. It lists six distinct groups and distinguishes between the fate of apostates and other sinners. Understanding this classification helps clarify the scope of intercession and the seriousness of certain sins and innovations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Get a sense of the author's straightforward enumeration.
Notice how the passage begins with 'فالمرتد من المطرودين' and proceeds to list groups.
2
Identify the six categories
Identify each distinct group mentioned: apostates, religious innovators, those who oppose the Muslim community (with examples), unjust oppressors, open sinners, and people of deviation and innovation.
The passage uses 'و' (and) to connect some categories, so look for the listing pattern.
3
Note the distinction between 'changers'
Recognize the final sentences that distinguish between 'the changer by apostasy' (eternal fire) and 'the changer by sins' (under God's will).
This distinction is crucial for understanding the fate of different groups.
4
Reflect on the severity of innovators
Observe that the passage says the Khawarij, Rawafid, and Mu'tazila are 'more severely expelled' than others. Reflect on why that might be.
The author calls them 'changers' (مبدلون), implying they altered the religion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالمرتد من المطرودين ، ومَن أحدث في الدِّين ما لا يرضاه الله تعالى ، ومَن خالف جماعة المسلمين ؛ كالخوارج والروافض والمعتزلة على اختلاف فرقهم، لأنَّهم مُبدِّلون بل هم أشدُّ طرداً مِن غيرهم، والظُّلمة الجائرون، والمُعلِنُ بالكبائر المُستخِفُّ بالمعاصي، وأهل الزيغ والبدع، لكن المُبدِّلُ بالارتداد مخلد في النار ، والمبدل بالمعاصي في المشيئة، والله أعلم.
The apostate is among the expelled, and whoever introduces into the religion what Allah does not approve, and whoever opposes the community of Muslims; like the Khawarij, Rawafid, and Mu'tazila with their different sects, because they are changers, rather they are more severely expelled than others, and the unjust oppressors, and those who openly commit major sins and make light of disobedience, and people of deviation and innovation. But the changer by apostasy is eternally in the Fire, and the changer by sins is under [God's] will. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a classification of those who are denied the Prophet's intercession. It lists six groups: apostates, religious innovators, those who oppose the Muslim community (citing specific examples: Khawarij, Rawafid, Mu'tazila), unjust oppressors, open sinners who are contemptuous of disobedience, and people of deviation and innovation. The commentator then distinguishes between two types of 'changers': those who change by apostasy (eternal punishment) and those who change by sins (subject to God's will). The passage emphasizes that the innovators among the sects are more severely expelled than others. The phrase 'in the will' (fi al-mashiyya) means their ultimate fate depends on God's decision—He may punish or forgive them, but apostates are unequivocally punished eternally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All sinners are automatically denied the Prophet's intercession.
Correction: The passage specifies particular categories: apostates, innovators, oppressors, open sinners who scorn disobedience, and people of deviation. Others who commit sins are under God's will and may receive intercession.

Checkpoint

A) Apostates
B) Open sinners
C) Khawarij, Rawafid, and Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intercession is denied to specific categories of people, with apostates facing eternal punishment while other sinners are subject to God's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you treat any sin lightly, thinking it is small? The passage warns against those who 'openly commit major sins and make light of disobedience.' Is there a sin you have normalized in your life? What will you do today to repent and change?
?
The passage includes 'whoever introduces into the religion what Allah does not approve.' Have you ever followed a practice or belief without verifying its source from the Qur'an and Sunnah? What step will you take to ensure your worship is pure and based on revelation?
?
Consider the category 'those who oppose the community of Muslims.' Are you part of any group or mindset that fosters division or sectarianism? How can you actively work to prioritize unity and avoid being among those who split the community?

The Obligation of Believing in Intercession
Proves obligation of intercession and lists three required beliefs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in the Prophet's intercession is obligatory and what three specific beliefs it entails.

Core Idea
Intercession is a revealed truth requiring three specific beliefs.

Sanusi now turns to another type of revealed matter: intercession. He states that belief in the Prophet's intercession is obligatory by revelation and consensus. But this belief is not simple; it includes three essential components that every Muslim must affirm.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on intercession
Read the Arabic passage once, noticing that it begins by establishing intercession as a revealed matter (sam'iy) and then lists three obligations.
Intercession is not rationally known; it is based on divine revelation.
2
Identify the three obligatory beliefs
The passage outlines three things that must be believed: that the Prophet is an intercessor, that his intercession is accepted, and that he is given precedence over all creation.
Each of these is a distinct component of the belief in intercession.
3
Reflect on the role of consensus
Notice that Sanusi mentions consensus before the rise of innovators, emphasizing that this belief is universally accepted by early Muslims.
This counters those who deny intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم شرع في نوع آخر من السمعيات وردت به الآثار، وانعقد عليه الإجماع قبل ظهور المبتدعة، فقال: (وَوَاجِبٌ) سمعا عندنا أهل الحق (شَفَاعَةُ المُشَفّع) (مُحَمَّدٍ) والشفاعة لغة: الوسيلة والطلب، وعرفا: سؤال الخير للغير. وفي كلامه إشارة إلى واجبات ثلاثة يتعيَّنُ اعتقادها على كل مكلَّف:
قسم السمعيات
فالأول: كونه صلى الله عليه وسلم شَافِعًا. والثاني: كونه صلى الله عليه وسلم مُشَفعًا، أي: مَقبُولَ الشفاعة. والثالث: كونه مُقَدَّمًا على غيره من جميع الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة المقربين. فيتعيّنُ اعتقاد أنَّه وإن كان له شَفاعات إلَّا أنَّ أعظمها: شفاعته العظمى المختصَّةُ به؛ للإراحة مِن طُول المَوقِف، وهي: أول المقام المحمود. ثانيها: في إدخال قوم الجنَّةَ بغير حساب، وهي مختصة به قاله النَّوويُّ. ثالثها: فيمن استحق دخول النار أن لا يدخلها، وتردَّد النَّوويُّ.
Then he began another type of revealed matters (sam'iyyat) that have come through traditions, and consensus was established upon it before the emergence of innovators. He said: 'And obligatory' by revelation according to us the people of truth (is) the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted, Muhammad. Intercession linguistically means mediation and request, and technically it is asking for good for someone else. In his words there is indication of three obligations that must be believed by every legally responsible person: Section of Revealed Matters. The first: that he (peace be upon him) is an intercessor. The second: that he (peace be upon him) is one whose intercession is accepted, i.e., his intercession is received. The third: that he is given precedence over others from all prophets, messengers, and the closest angels. So it is necessary to believe that although he has intercessions, the greatest of them is his great intercession specific to him; for relief from the length of the standing, and it is the first of the praiseworthy station. The second: in causing some people to enter Paradise without reckoning, and it is specific to him, according to al-Nawawi. The third: for those who deserve to enter the Fire that they not enter it, and al-Nawawi hesitated.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a proof and classification of the obligation of believing in the Prophet's intercession. It begins by stating that this topic is from the revealed matters (sam'iyyat) established by traditions and consensus before the rise of innovators. The verse 'And obligatory by revelation' indicates that intercession is not rationally necessary but divinely commanded. The passage then extracts three obligatory beliefs from the line: 1) The Prophet is an intercessor, 2) His intercession is accepted, 3) He is given precedence over all other prophets, messengers, and angels. After establishing these beliefs, the passage enumerates three types of his intercession: (a) the greatest intercession for relief from the long standing on the Day of Judgment—this is specific to him and is the first part of the Praiseworthy Station (al-maqam al-mahmud); (b) the intercession for admitting some people to Paradise without reckoning—al-Nawawi affirms its exclusivity to the Prophet; (c) the intercession for those who deserve Hellfire to prevent them from entering—al-Nawawi hesitated on whether this is exclusive. The passage emphasizes that belief in these is required of every legally responsible person.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
المُشَفّع
السمعيات
الإجماع
المبتدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that belief in intercession is optional or that it is sufficient to simply affirm it without specific components.
Correction: The passage shows that intercession is obligatory by revelation and requires affirming three distinct beliefs: the Prophet as intercessor, acceptance of his intercession, and his precedence over all creation.

Checkpoint
What does the phrase 'waajibun sama'an' (obligatory by revelation) indicate about the basis for believing in intercession?
A) It is rationally necessary
B) It is based on divine revelation and tradition
C) It is optional
D) It is derived from consensus only

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Prophet's intercession is obligatory and includes affirming his role as intercessor, that his intercession is accepted, and his precedence over all creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly and wholeheartedly believe that the Prophet Muhammad’s intercession is accepted by Allah—not just as a theoretical possibility, but as a real event that will happen? What evidence in your daily life shows that you rely on this belief?
?
When you think about your sins and shortcomings, do you ever feel that the Prophet’s intercession is 'too good to be true' or that it might not apply to someone like you? How does this passage challenge that feeling?
?
The third belief is that the Prophet is given precedence over all prophets, messengers, and angels. Does your heart truly place him above all others in love and reverence? In what ways do you fall short of giving him that supreme status in your thoughts, words, and actions?

The Three Types of the Prophet's Intercession
Enumerates three types of the Prophet's intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct types of the Prophet's intercession and which ones are specific to him.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession has three types, with the greatest being universal and two others unique to him.

Having established the obligation to believe in intercession, Sanusi now details the specific types. He explains that while the Prophet has multiple intercessions, the most important is his great intercession on the Day of Judgment, followed by intercession for entering Paradise without reckoning and for preventing entry to Hell.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of the three types
Read the passage carefully, noting that each type is introduced with a number: first, second, third.
The first type is called the 'great intercession'.
2
Identify the purpose of each intercession
The first relieves the standing, the second admits people to Paradise without reckoning, the third prevents entry to Hell.
Al-Nawawi’s opinion on exclusivity varies for each.
3
Distinguish between the types
Notice that the first two are explicitly stated as specific to the Prophet, while al-Nawawi hesitated on the third.
This shows scholarly debate on the scope of intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم شرع في نوع آخر من السمعيات وردت به الآثار، وانعقد عليه الإجماع قبل ظهور المبتدعة، فقال: (وَوَاجِبٌ) سمعا عندنا أهل الحق (شَفَاعَةُ المُشَفّع) (مُحَمَّدٍ) والشفاعة لغة: الوسيلة والطلب، وعرفا: سؤال الخير للغير. وفي كلامه إشارة إلى واجبات ثلاثة يتعيَّنُ اعتقادها على كل مكلَّف:
قسم السمعيات
فالأول: كونه صلى الله عليه وسلم شَافِعًا. والثاني: كونه صلى الله عليه وسلم مُشَفعًا، أي: مَقبُولَ الشفاعة. والثالث: كونه مُقَدَّمًا على غيره من جميع الأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة المقربين. فيتعيّنُ اعتقاد أنَّه وإن كان له شَفاعات إلَّا أنَّ أعظمها: شفاعته العظمى المختصَّةُ به؛ للإراحة مِن طُول المَوقِف، وهي: أول المقام المحمود. ثانيها: في إدخال قوم الجنَّةَ بغير حساب، وهي مختصة به قاله النَّوويُّ. ثالثها: فيمن استحق دخول النار أن لا يدخلها، وتردَّد النَّوويُّ.
Then he began another type of revealed matters (sam'iyyat) that have come through traditions, and consensus was established upon it before the emergence of innovators. He said: 'And obligatory' by revelation according to us the people of truth (is) the intercession of the one whose intercession is accepted, Muhammad. Intercession linguistically means mediation and request, and technically it is asking for good for someone else. In his words there is indication of three obligations that must be believed by every legally responsible person: Section of Revealed Matters. The first: that he (peace be upon him) is an intercessor. The second: that he (peace be upon him) is one whose intercession is accepted, i.e., his intercession is received. The third: that he is given precedence over others from all prophets, messengers, and the closest angels. So it is necessary to believe that although he has intercessions, the greatest of them is his great intercession specific to him; for relief from the length of the standing, and it is the first of the praiseworthy station. The second: in causing some people to enter Paradise without reckoning, and it is specific to him, according to al-Nawawi. The third: for those who deserve to enter the Fire that they not enter it, and al-Nawawi hesitated.
Source pages p. 554

Commentary
This passage is a proof and classification of the obligation of believing in the Prophet's intercession. It begins by stating that this topic is from the revealed matters (sam'iyyat) established by traditions and consensus before the rise of innovators. The verse 'And obligatory by revelation' indicates that intercession is not rationally necessary but divinely commanded. The passage then extracts three obligatory beliefs from the line: 1) The Prophet is an intercessor, 2) His intercession is accepted, 3) He is given precedence over all other prophets, messengers, and angels. After establishing these beliefs, the passage enumerates three types of his intercession: (a) the greatest intercession for relief from the long standing on the Day of Judgment—this is specific to him and is the first part of the Praiseworthy Station (al-maqam al-mahmud); (b) the intercession for admitting some people to Paradise without reckoning—al-Nawawi affirms its exclusivity to the Prophet; (c) the intercession for those who deserve Hellfire to prevent them from entering—al-Nawawi hesitated on whether this is exclusive. The passage emphasizes that belief in these is required of every legally responsible person.

Key Terms
المقام المحمود
مختصة
النووي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession is a single event on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: The passage shows that intercession has multiple distinct types with different purposes and scopes, including intercession for relief, for entering Paradise without reckoning, and for preventing entry to Hell.

Checkpoint
Which type of intercession does al-Nawawi affirm as specific to the Prophet?
A) The greatest intercession for relief
B) Intercession for entering Paradise without reckoning
C) Intercession for preventing entry to Hell
D) All intercessions

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intercession has three distinct types: the greatest for relief, for entering Paradise without reckoning, and for preventing entry to Hell; the first two are specific to him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
The passage shows that some intercessions are unique to the Prophet yet you still gamble on vague hopes. Have you ever thanked Allah for granting this nation such a Prophet? Write down one genuine expression of gratitude that you will utter in your next prayer.

The Fourth Type of Intercession: Bringing Monotheists out of Hell
Enumeration of the fourth type of intercession with a condition from Qadi 'Iyad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth type of intercession: bringing monotheists out of Hell, and the condition for its exclusivity to the Prophet according to Qadi 'Iyad.

Core Idea
Intercession for believers with minimal faith is the Prophet's exclusive gift.

This lesson explores the fourth type of the Prophet’s intercession, which concerns those monotheists who are in the Fire. Qadi 'Iyad offers a key distinction: if the person has only an atom of faith with no good deeds, the Prophet alone intercedes; otherwise, others share in the intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the classification.
2
Identify the distinction
Notice the condition set by Qadi 'Iyad: the intercession is exclusive if the person has no good deeds besides faith.
This is a nuanced point.
3
Reflect on implications
Consider why this distinction matters for understanding the scope of the Prophet's role.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في اختصاصها به . أنواع شفاعته رابعها: في إخراج الموحدين مِن النَّار، ويُشاركه في هذه الأنبياء والملائكة والمؤمنونَ ، وفَصَّل القاضي عياض فقال: إن كانت هذه الشفاعة لإخراج من في قلبه مثقالُ ذَرَّةٍ مِن إيمان اختصت به ، ولا يُشاركه غيره، وإلَّا شارَكَهُ فيها غيره . خَامِسُهَا: في زيادة الدرجات في الجنَّة لأهلها ، وجوز النَّوويُّ اختصاصها به . سادسُها في جماعةٍ مِن صُلحَاءِ أَمَّته ؛ ليتجاوز عنهم في تقصيرهم في الطاعات . سابعها: فيمن خُلد في النَّارِ مِن الكفر أن يخفف عنهم العذاب في أوقاتٍ مخصوصة كما في حق أبي طالب وأبي لهب وغيره . ثامنها: في أطفال المشركين أنْ لا يُعذَّبوا ذكره جلال الدين السيوطي
In its exclusivity to him. Types of his intercession. Fourth: In bringing out the monotheists from the Fire, and he shares in this with the prophets, angels, and believers, and Qadi 'Iyad detailed saying: If this intercession is for bringing out one who has in his heart the weight of an atom of faith, it is exclusive to him and no one else shares with him; otherwise, others share with him. Fifth: In increasing degrees in Paradise for its people, and al-Nawawi permitted its exclusivity to him. Sixth: In a group of the righteous of his ummah, so that they be pardoned for their shortcomings in acts of obedience. Seventh: In those who are eternally in the Fire of disbelief, that the punishment be lightened for them at specific times, as in the case of Abu Talib and Abu Lahab and others. Eighth: Concerning the children of polytheists, that they not be punished; mentioned by Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the types of the Prophet's intercession (shafa'ah), continuing an earlier enumeration. It lists four specific types (fourth to eighth). The fourth type is for bringing monotheists out of Hell; Qadi 'Iyad distinguishes whether the intercession is exclusive to the Prophet or shared based on the presence of additional good deeds. The fifth type is increasing degrees in Paradise, considered exclusive by al-Nawawi. The sixth type is for a group of righteous people to be pardoned for shortcomings. The seventh type concerns lightening the punishment for eternally damned disbelievers at specific times, citing Abu Talib and Abu Lahab. The eighth type, mentioned by al-Suyuti, is that the children of polytheists will not be punished. The author follows the classification order and includes details from renowned scholars.

Key Terms
شفاعة
موحدين
النار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that all intercession for entering Paradise is exclusive to the Prophet.
Correction: In this type, the Prophet shares intercession with others unless the person has no good deeds, in which case it is exclusive.

Checkpoint

B) When the person has only the weight of an atom of faith without additional good deeds

D) Never exclusive

Key Takeaway
The Prophet has a unique intercession for monotheists with minimal faith, but his intercession is shared with others when good deeds are present.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Eighth Type of Intercession: Children of Polytheists Not Punished
Enumeration of the eighth type attributed to al-Suyuti.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the eighth type of intercession: that the children of polytheists will not be punished, as mentioned by al-Suyuti.

Core Idea
The Prophet intercedes for the children of polytheists to be spared from punishment.

This lesson covers the eighth and final type of intercession mentioned here: that the children of polytheists will not be punished. This view is attributed to Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti. It addresses the fate of young children who died before reaching the age of accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the description of the eighth type.
2
Identify the recipients
The children of polytheists (mushrikin).
3
Note the source
This is attributed to al-Suyuti.
This indicates it may not be universally accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في اختصاصها به . أنواع شفاعته رابعها: في إخراج الموحدين مِن النَّار، ويُشاركه في هذه الأنبياء والملائكة والمؤمنونَ ، وفَصَّل القاضي عياض فقال: إن كانت هذه الشفاعة لإخراج من في قلبه مثقالُ ذَرَّةٍ مِن إيمان اختصت به ، ولا يُشاركه غيره، وإلَّا شارَكَهُ فيها غيره . خَامِسُهَا: في زيادة الدرجات في الجنَّة لأهلها ، وجوز النَّوويُّ اختصاصها به . سادسُها في جماعةٍ مِن صُلحَاءِ أَمَّته ؛ ليتجاوز عنهم في تقصيرهم في الطاعات . سابعها: فيمن خُلد في النَّارِ مِن الكفر أن يخفف عنهم العذاب في أوقاتٍ مخصوصة كما في حق أبي طالب وأبي لهب وغيره . ثامنها: في أطفال المشركين أنْ لا يُعذَّبوا ذكره جلال الدين السيوطي
In its exclusivity to him. Types of his intercession. Fourth: In bringing out the monotheists from the Fire, and he shares in this with the prophets, angels, and believers, and Qadi 'Iyad detailed saying: If this intercession is for bringing out one who has in his heart the weight of an atom of faith, it is exclusive to him and no one else shares with him; otherwise, others share with him. Fifth: In increasing degrees in Paradise for its people, and al-Nawawi permitted its exclusivity to him. Sixth: In a group of the righteous of his ummah, so that they be pardoned for their shortcomings in acts of obedience. Seventh: In those who are eternally in the Fire of disbelief, that the punishment be lightened for them at specific times, as in the case of Abu Talib and Abu Lahab and others. Eighth: Concerning the children of polytheists, that they not be punished; mentioned by Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti.
Source pages p. 556

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the types of the Prophet's intercession (shafa'ah), continuing an earlier enumeration. It lists four specific types (fourth to eighth). The fourth type is for bringing monotheists out of Hell; Qadi 'Iyad distinguishes whether the intercession is exclusive to the Prophet or shared based on the presence of additional good deeds. The fifth type is increasing degrees in Paradise, considered exclusive by al-Nawawi. The sixth type is for a group of righteous people to be pardoned for shortcomings. The seventh type concerns lightening the punishment for eternally damned disbelievers at specific times, citing Abu Talib and Abu Lahab. The eighth type, mentioned by al-Suyuti, is that the children of polytheists will not be punished. The author follows the classification order and includes details from renowned scholars.

شفاعة
أطفال المشركين

B) That children of polytheists not be punished
C) That children of polytheists be sent to Paradise
D) That children of polytheists be spared from Hell

Key Takeaway
The eighth intercession spares the children of polytheists from punishment, as per al-Suyuti.

Intercession of Other Righteous Figures
Affirmation that prophets, angels, and saints intercede for major sinners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that intercession is not limited to the Prophet Muhammad alone but includes other chosen righteous figures such as prophets, angels, companions, martyrs, and saints.

Core Idea
Many righteous intercede for major sinners—not just the Prophet.

This short but significant passage expands our understanding of intercession. The verse affirms that not only the Prophet Muhammad but also other chosen righteous figures intercede for major sinners. The commentary explains who these figures include and bases this on authentic reports and Sunni consensus. This lesson will help you appreciate the breadth of divine mercy.

Refuting the Mu'tazila Denial of Intercession
Explains 'la tamna' and refutes Mu'tazila denial of intercession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why denying the Prophet's intercession for major sinners is prohibited and how the Sunni response refutes the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
Intercession for major sinners is a mercy that cannot be denied.

This passage addresses a critical point of difference between Sunni Islam and the Mu'tazila: whether the Prophet's intercession can benefit major sinners. The author clarifies the meaning of 'do not prevent' and refutes a hadith used to deny intercession, showing that it is fabricated or misinterpreted.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice the concise style and the key terms like shafā‘ah, ahl al-kabā’ir, and mu‘tazila.
2
Understand the meaning of 'la tamna'
The phrase 'la tamna' is interpreted as prohibiting the belief that intercession is impossible. Identify that this denial is characteristic of the Mu‘tazila and that the intercession applies to major sinners both before and after entering the Fire.
This directly refutes the Mu‘tazila stance that major sinners deserve eternal punishment without intercession.
3
Examine the hadith argument and its refutation
The Mu‘tazila cite a hadith denying intercession for major sinners. The author declares it unanimously fabricated, and even assuming authenticity, restricts it to apostates. Notice the two-tier refutation: complete rejection followed by conditional interpretation.
This shows the Sunni method of defending doctrine by critically assessing the sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقصد بقوله : (لَا تَمْنَع) أي: لا تعتقد امتناع شفاعته صلى الله عليه وسلم في أهل الكبائر ،وغيرهم لا قبل دخولهم النَّار ولا بعده.. الرَّدَّ على المعتزلة ومن وافقهم، وحديث: «لا تَنالُ شفاعتي أهل الكبائرِ مِن أُمَّتِي» مَوْضوع باتفاق ، وبتقدير صحته : هو محمول على من ارتدَّ منهم.
And by His saying: 'Do not prevent' meaning: do not believe the impossibility of his intercession, may God bless him and grant him peace, for the people of major sins, and others, neither before their entry into the Fire nor after it. It is a refutation of the Mu'tazila and those who agree with them. The hadith: 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my nation' is unanimously fabricated, and assuming its authenticity, it is interpreted as referring to those who apostatized from them.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the phrase 'la tamna' (do not prevent). The commentator explains that the intended meaning is the prohibition of denying the possibility of the Prophet's intercession for major sinners. This denial is characteristic of the Mu'tazila, who argue that grave sinners deserve eternal punishment. The commentator then refutes a key evidence used by the Mu'tazila: the hadith 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my nation.' He declares this hadith to be unanimously fabricated (mawḍū‘). He further states that even if one were to presume its authenticity, it must be interpreted as referring to apostates, not to Muslims who commit major sins. Thus, the passage defends the Sunni doctrine of intercession for major sinners.

Misconception: The hadith 'لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي' is authentic and proves that the Prophet's intercession does not benefit major sinners.
Correction: The hadith is unanimously fabricated. Even if assumed authentic, it applies only to apostates, not to Muslims who commit major sins.

Intercession of Other Chosen Beings
Explains the scope of intercession beyond the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Sunni doctrine, intercession is not limited to the Prophet Muhammad but includes other righteous beings such as prophets, angels, saints, etc., and that their intercession occurs only after the completion of punishment.

Core Idea
Intercession is not exclusive; many chosen beings intercede by God's permission.

This passage from the Jawharat al-Tawhid explains a key Sunni belief that intercession (shafa'a) is granted not only to the Prophet but to many other righteous beings. It clarifies who these intercessors are and the condition under which they intercede. Let's read the source directly.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the translation to understand the literal meaning.
The passage includes both the matn and its commentary.
2
Identify the list of intercessors
The passage names several groups who intercede. Make a mental list: prophets, messengers, angels, Companions, martyrs, righteous, saints.
3
Note the proof and conditions
The proof is from hadith and consensus of Ahl al-Sunna, and the condition is that intercession occurs only after the period of punishment.
This guards against the misunderstanding that intercession happens immediately.
4
Reflect on the inclusion of Allah
The commentator includes Allah as an intercessor for those who said 'La ilaha illa Allah' with no good deeds. Consider how this expands the concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شفاعة غيره من الأنبياء والأولياء 
 وَغَيْرُهُ مِنْ مُرْتَضَى الأَخْيَارِ يَشْفَعُ كَمَا قَدْ جَاءَ فِي الْأَخْبَارِ 
 (وَغَيْرُه)، أي: ويجبُ أنْ يَعتقد أنَّ غيرَهُ صلى الله عليه وسلم (مِنْ مُرْتَضَى الأَخْيَارِ) كالأنبياء والمرسلين والملائكة والصَّحابة، والشُّهداء، والصالحين، والأولياء ، (يَشْفَعُ) على قَدْرِ مَقامِه عند الله في أرباب الكبائر (كما)، أي: للحديث الَّذي قَدْ جَاءَ فِي الأَخْبَارِ الدَّالَّة على ذلك ، مما أجمع عليه أهل السُّنَّة ، ودخل في الغير الشَّافِعِ الله ، فإِنَّه يَشْفَعُ فيمن قالَ: لا إله إلا الله ، ولم يعمل خيرا قط ، والملائكة أيضا ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يَشْفَعُونَ إِلَّا لِمَنِ ارْتَضَى﴾ [الأنبياء: ۲۸] . فيشفعون فيمن كانَ على مكارم الأخلاق مِن بني آدم ، ولا يشفعُ واحدٌ ممَّن ذكرنا إلَّا بعد انتهاء مُدَّة المؤاخذة.
Intercession of other than him from the prophets and saints. And other than him from the chosen good ones intercedes as has come in the reports. (And other than him) i.e., it is obligatory to believe that other than him, may God bless him and grant him peace, from the chosen good ones like the prophets and messengers and angels and Companions and martyrs and righteous and saints, intercedes according to his station with God for the people of major sins, as (i.e., because of) the hadith that has come in the reports indicating that, which the people of the Sunna have agreed upon. And included in 'other than him' is God, the Intercessor, for He intercedes for one who says 'There is no god but God' and has never done any good; and also the angels, because of His statement, the Exalted: 'And they do not intercede except for whom He is pleased with' [Quran 21:28]. So they intercede for those who possess noble character from the children of Adam, and none of those we mentioned intercedes except after the completion of the period of punishment.
Source pages p. 557

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the doctrine that intercession is not limited to the Prophet Muhammad but includes other righteous beings. It begins with a heading and the poetic line (matn) stating that 'other than him' from the chosen good ones intercede. The commentator then explains that it is obligatory to believe that other created beings—specifically enumerated as prophets, messengers, angels, Companions, martyrs, righteous, and saints—intercede for major sinners according to their rank with God. The proof is the reports (ahādīth) that have come, which the Ahl al-Sunna have unanimously accepted. The commentator adds that even God Himself is included as an intercessor in a certain sense, for He intercedes for someone who merely uttered 'Lā ilāha illā Allāh' without any good deeds. The angels also intercede, based on the Qur'anic verse that they only intercede for those God is pleased with. However, the commentator specifies that intercession by any of these occurs only after the period of punishment (mu’ākhadha) is completed, meaning for those already in Hellfire to be released or for their punishment to be lifted.

Rational Proof for Intercession: Forgiveness of Non-Kufr Sins
Presents rational argument that forgiveness of non-kufr sins justifies intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational basis for intercession in Sunni theology: that since God can forgive sins other than disbelief, intercession is possible and we do not excommunicate believers for sin.

Core Idea
If God can forgive sins that are not disbelief, then intercession for such sins is plausible.

This lesson presents a concise but powerful rational argument for the doctrine of intercession. The theologian asserts that the very possibility of God forgiving sins other than disbelief provides a logical foundation for intercession, and thus we must not declare a believer an unbeliever due to sin. The commentator clarifies that intercession, though established by revelation, also rests on this rational proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic heading, matn line, and commentator’s note. Then read the literal translation to grasp the surface meaning.
The passage is short but dense.
2
Identify the key premise
Find the phrase 'إذ جائز غفران غير الكفر' (forgiveness of other than disbelief is possible). This is the rational foundation.
3
Understand the conclusion
Notice the immediate consequence: 'فلا نكفر مؤمنا بالوزر' (we do not declare a believer a disbeliever because of sin). This refutes excommunication for major sins.
4
Connect to intercession
The commentator states that intercession has a rational proof indicated by this line. Reflect on how the possibility of forgiveness opens the door for prophetic intercession.
Consider the opposing Mu'tazilite view that major sins cause eternal punishment.
5
Review the misconception
Recognize that the passage directly counters the wrong belief that major sins make a person a disbeliever.
This is a key point of Sunni creed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان أن غفران غير الكفر مسوغ للشفاعة 
 إِذْ جَائِزٌ غُفْرانُ غَيْرِ الكُفْرِ فلا نُكَفِّرْ مُؤْمِنًا بالوِزْرِ 
 والشفاعة وإن كانت واجبةً شرعًا إلَّا أنَّ لها دليلًا عقليًّا أشار إليه
Clarification that forgiveness of other than disbelief is a justification for intercession. For the forgiveness of other than disbelief is possible, so we do not declare a believer a disbeliever because of sin. And intercession, even if it is legally obligatory, yet it has a rational proof indicated by it.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a proof and classification. It begins with a heading: 'Clarification that forgiveness of other than disbelief is a justification for intercession.' The poetic line (matn) states the rational foundation: since the forgiveness of sins that are not disbelief is possible (jā’iz) in God's power, we do not excommunicate a believer due to sin (i.e., we do not say a believer becomes a kāfir solely because of committing a major sin). The commentator then adds that intercession, while being legally obligatory (wājib shar‘an), also has a rational proof, which is indicated by this very line. In other words, the possibility of forgiving non-kufr sins is the rational basis that validates the doctrine of intercession. If God can forgive such sins directly, there is no barrier to His accepting the intercession of His prophets and saints for the same purpose. This rational argument refutes the Mu'tazilite position that major sins necessitate eternal punishment, thereby ruling out intercession.

Key Terms
الغفران
الكفر
الوزر
الشَفاعة
دليل عقلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Committing a major sin makes a person a disbeliever.
Correction: The passage clarifies that sin (الوزر) does not remove faith; a believer remains a believer even if guilty of major sins, because forgiveness of such sins is possible.

Checkpoint
What is the rational proof for intercession mentioned in the passage?
A) The Prophet's intercession is mentioned in many hadiths.
B) It is legally obligatory, so no rational proof is needed.
C) Since forgiveness of sins other than disbelief is possible, intercession is plausible.
D) Intercession is necessary to maintain social order.

Key Takeaway
The possibility of God forgiving sins other than disbelief provides the rational foundation for intercession and refutes the claim that major sins cause excommunication.

Rational Basis for Intercession
Commentator explains rational basis for intercession via forgiveness possibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the rational possibility of forgiving non-kufr sins provides a rational basis for the permissibility of intercession, and that intercession is both legally obligatory and rationally acceptable.

Core Idea
Forgiveness of non-kufr sins is rationally possible, making intercession appropriate and necessary.

In this passage, the commentator explains a key point from the matn: since it is rationally permissible for God to forgive sins other than disbelief, intercession is not prevented either legally or rationally. He unpacks the rational proof and shows that intercession, though legally obligatory, also has a rational grounding. Let's explore how this argument works.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the commentator's argument.
Notice the flow from the matn line to the commentator's explanation.
2
Identify the rational proof
The commentator states that forgiveness of non-kufr sins is rationally permissible. This is the key rational basis. Find where he explains this.
The phrase 'since it is permissible' links back to the matn.
3
Understand the implication for intercession
Because forgiveness of non-kufr sins is possible, intercession, which is a means to that forgiveness, is even more appropriate and must be accepted legally and rationally.
The commentator emphasizes that intercession is not impossible and is among the possibilities of the intellect.

إِذْ جَائِزٌ غُفْرانُ غَيْرِ الكُفْرِ فلا نُكَفِّرْ مُؤْمِنًا بالوِزْرِ

والشَّفاعة وإن كانت واجبةً شرعًا إلَّا أنَّ لها دليلًا عقليًّا أشار إليه بقوله: (إِذْ جَائِزُ) الواقع علة لقوله: لا الشفاعة تمنع يعني: لا تمنع شرعاً؛ لما ورد مِن إثباتها، ولا عقلا لأنَّه يجوز عقلا وسمعا عليه تعالى تفضلا وإحسانًا: (غُفْرَانُ غَيْرِ الكُفْرِ) مِن الذُّنوب بلا توبةٍ ولا شَفاعة، فبالشَّفاعة أَوْلى؛ لأنَّها ليست مُستحيلةٌ، بل مِن مُجوّزات العقولِ، وكلّ ما هو كذلك، فهو واجبُ القَبول ممتنعُ الرَّد شرعاً. وبيان جوازها: أنَّ العقلَ يُجوِّزُ على الله تعالى أن يعفو عن الصغائر مطلقا، وعن الكبائر بعد التّوبة قطعاً، وبدونها إن شاء، ولا يعفو عن الكُفر قطعاً؛ لدليل السمع، وإن جاز عقلا على الأصح، هذا ما اتفقت عليه الأمة، ونطق به الكتاب والسنة.
Since the forgiveness of other than kufr (disbelief) is permissible, we do not declare a believer an unbeliever for his sin. And intercession, although it is obligatory by law, yet it has a rational proof indicated by his saying: 'Since it is permissible' — which is the cause for his saying: 'Intercession is not prevented' meaning: it is not prevented legally due to what has come of its affirmation, nor rationally because it is rationally and scripturally permissible upon Him, exalted, as a favor and beneficence: 'Forgiveness of other than kufr' of sins without repentance and without intercession, then intercession is more appropriate because it is not impossible, but rather among the possibilities of the intellects, and everything that is like that, then it is obligatory to accept, impossible to reject legally. And the explanation of its permissibility: that the intellect permits upon God Almighty to forgive minor sins absolutely, and major sins after repentance definitively, and without it if He wills, and He does not forgive kufr definitively due to scriptural evidence, even if it is rationally permissible according to the most correct view. This is what the community has agreed upon, and the Book and Sunnah have spoken with it.
Source pages p. 558

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn line 'Since the forgiveness of other than kufr is permissible, we do not declare a believer an unbeliever for his sin.' The commentator first states that intercession is obligatory by Islamic law, but it also has a rational proof. He explains that the matn line provides this proof: the phrase 'since it is permissible' is the cause for saying that intercession is not prevented. It is not prevented legally because there is scriptural evidence affirming it, nor rationally because it is rationally and scripturally permissible for God to forgive sins other than kufr as a favor. The commentator clarifies that forgiveness of sins without repentance or intercession is possible, so intercession is even more appropriate since it is not impossible. Anything that is rationally possible and affirmed by revelation must be accepted and cannot be rejected. He then explains the rational basis: the intellect permits God to forgive minor sins absolutely, and major sins after repentance definitively, and without repentance if He wills, but He does not forgive kufr definitively based on scriptural evidence, even if it is rationally permissible. He concludes that this is the consensus of the community and is attested by the Quran and Sunnah.

Forgiveness of Non-Kufr Sins: Rational and Legal Basis
Commentator explains the permissibility of forgiveness of sins other than kufr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why forgiveness of sins other than disbelief is permissible both rationally and according to revelation, and the conditions for that forgiveness.

Core Idea
Forgiveness of non-kufr sins is rationally possible and legally confirmed.

This passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawheed addresses a key question in Islamic theology: Can Allah forgive sins without repentance or intercession? The author, al-Laqqani, clarifies that while disbelief is definitively not forgiven, other sins—major and minor—fall within divine prerogative. The argument combines rational possibility with scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation once. Let the author's own words set the stage before analysis.
