Regarding acquisition (iktisab) and trust (tawakkul), there is disagreement, and the preponderant view is the detailed distinction (tafsil) according to what is known.
Sawm,
Then he mentioned an issue from mysticism (tasawwuf), some of whose forms will come later at the saying of the versifier: 'And be as were the best of creation', due to its connection with the topic of provision; because some of it is obtained without acquisition (1), and some of it is obtained by directly undertaking means (asbab) by choice. So he said: (Regarding acquisition) i.e., regarding its superiority (2), and it is directly undertaking means by choice, like traveling for profit, and taking medicine to obtain health or preserve it (3), and similar things. And (regarding) (trust) from the servant, which is: reliance upon Him, Exalted, and disregarding the means while they are prepared (4). And it is said: it is abandoning striving in what human ability does not encompass (5). (There is disagreement) (6) [concerning] superiority.
(1) His statement: (without acquisition without undertaking a cause, as was the case with Maryam bint 'Imran: in summer, winter fruits would come to her, and in winter, summer fruits, without anyone entering upon her. Al-Shanwani.)
(2) His statement: (i.e., regarding its superiority) is an indication that the discussion is intended to express a comparison. Al-Shanwani.
(3) His statement: (to obtain health) i.e., in the sick person when it is absent. And his statement: (or preserve it) i.e., in the healthy person when it is present. Al-Shanwani.
(4) His statement: (and disregarding the means) i.e., not relying on them. And his statement: (while they are prepared) i.e., being able to use them. Al-Shanwani.
(5) His statement: (and it is said: it is abandoning striving) i.e., although this is not intended here. His statement: (what human ability does not encompass) like flying, and it applies to striving in what humans can do like buying and selling. Al-Shanwani.
•
(6) His statement: (there is disagreement) and the purport of that from the two ways: that in the first way, trust (tawakkul) contradicts acquisition (iktisab) because it is its opposite according to the proponent of that way, who is Abu Ja'far al-Tabari and those who agree with him. As for the way...
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage begins a new subsection on the relationship between acquisition (iktisab) and trust (tawakkul). The opening line is a poetic statement: 'Regarding acquisition and trust, there is disagreement, and the preponderant view is the detailed distinction according to what is known.' Al-Bajuri then explains that the poet (al-Laqqani) introduces this issue because of its connection to provision: some provision comes without any effort (like the provision of Maryam), while some comes through direct action. He then defines 'iktisab' as the direct undertaking of means by choice, giving examples like traveling for profit or taking medicine. He defines 'tawakkul' as reliance upon God while still preparing the means, and notes an alternative definition: abandoning striving in things beyond human capability (which is not the intended meaning here). The footnotes by al-Shanwani clarify that the discussion is about comparing the two, and that the first group (Abu Ja'far al-Tabari) holds that tawakkul and iktisab are contradictory — one negates the other. The passage cuts off before presenting the second group, but the preferred view (al-rajih) is the detailed distinction (tafsil), meaning that sometimes acquisition is better, sometimes trust is better, depending on the person and circumstances.

اكتساب
توكل
أفضلية
تفصيل
أسباب
مباشرة الأسباب
قطع النظر عن الأسباب

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawakkul means abandoning all worldly efforts and relying solely on God without any preparation.
Correction: The passage defines tawakkul as reliance on God while still preparing the means (مع تهيئها). Preparation is part of trust, not opposed to it.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The definitions of iktisab and tawakkul show that trust in God does not negate effort; the preponderant view is that the superiority of one over the other depends on the situation.

Two Scholarly Views on Kasb and Tawakkul
The author distinguishes two scholarly views on the relationship between earning (kasb) and trust (tawakkul).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly approaches to the relationship between earning (kasb) and trust in God (tawakkul), and why the majority view holds that earning does not contradict trust.

Core Idea
True trust in God does not forbid earning; it requires confidence in God while following the Prophet's sunna in seeking provision.

In this passage, the author presents a nuanced discussion about how earning a livelihood relates to relying on God. Some scholars held that earning contradicts trust, but the majority defined trust differently, allowing for earning as long as the heart remains reliant on God. Let's explore these two views.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text carefully, then read the literal translation to grasp the author's terms.
2
Identify the two scholarly approaches
Notice that the author mentions two ways (طريقين) among scholars. The first sees earning as contradicting trust; the second sees no contradiction.
3
Understand the second view's definition
The second view defines tawakkul as confidence in God, certainty in His decree, and following the sunna in seeking necessities. This allows earning.
4
Reflect on the practical implication
Consider how this understanding balances spiritual reliance with worldly effort, as exemplified by the prophets.
This aligns with the Ash'ari position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالاكتسابُ في حقَّهُ أَرجحُ حذرًا من التسخط وعدم الصبر، بل ربما وجب التكسب في حقه، وهذا التفصيل حسبما عرف من كتب القوم، كالإحياء للغزالي، والرسالة للقشيري. ولكن هذا التفصيل لا يتمشى إلا على أحد طريقي العلماء: أن الاكتساب ينافي التوكل، وأما على الطريق الثاني الراجح عند الجمهور: فلا؛ لأنهم عرفوا التوكل بأنه: الثقة بالله تعالى، والإيقان بأن قضاءه نافذ، واتباع سنة نبيه في السعي فيما لا بد منه سيما المطعم والمشرب والتحرز من العدو، كما فعله الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام.
But earning is more preponderant in his case, out of fear of discontent and lack of patience; rather, earning may even become obligatory in his case. This detailed ruling is as known from the books of the people, such as al-Ihya' by al-Ghazali and al-Risala by al-Qushayri. However, this detailed ruling only applies according to one of the two ways of the scholars: that earning contradicts trust. As for the second way, which is preponderant with the majority, it does not; because they defined trust as: confidence in God Almighty, and certainty that His decree is executive, and following the Sunnah of His Prophet in striving for what is necessary, especially food and drink and guarding against the enemy, as the prophets did, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage is a classification of two scholarly positions on the relationship between kasb (earning) and tawakkul (trust in God). The author first mentions a detailed ruling about when earning is recommended or obligatory based on a person's spiritual state. Then he explains that this detailed ruling only applies according to the first of two scholarly approaches, which holds that earning contradicts trust. According to the second approach, which is preponderant among the majority (the Ash'aris), earning does not contradict trust. They define tawakkul as inner confidence in God and certainty that His decree is executed, while still following the Prophet's sunna in seeking lawful provision and self-protection. Thus, the passage clarifies that true trust does not preclude engaging in permissible means.

B) Confidence in God while following the Prophet's sunna in seeking provision.

D) Only seeking provision through prayer.

Key Takeaway
The majority of scholars affirm that earning a lawful livelihood does not contradict trust in God; rather, trust is confidence in God while fulfilling worldly responsibilities as per the sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The passage warns that earning may become obligatory if one fears discontent. Which fear drives your earning: fear of poverty or fear of displeasing Allah? Make a concrete plan to purify your intention in your work this week.

The Sunni Doctrine on Major and Minor Sins
The commentator explains the Sunni position on the division of sins into major and minor, refuting other sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position on the division of sins into major and minor, the definitions and indicators of major sins, and how this view refutes the extremes of the Murji'ah and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Sins are divided into major and minor, and only specific major sins constitute disbelief.

The commentator begins by addressing the disagreement among Muslim sects regarding the nature of sins. He clarifies the Sunni stance that sins are indeed divided into major and minor categories, and this classification has clear indicators. This passage also refutes the positions of the Murji'ah, who downplay all sins, and the Khawarij, who exaggerate them into disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context of disagreement
Recognize that different sects had conflicting views on whether sins are divided and how severe they are. The Sunni position is presented as a middle path.
2
Learn the definition of sin
The passage defines sin (dhanb) and lists synonyms. This establishes the basic terminology.
3
Identify the refuted sects
The passage explicitly excludes Murji'ah and Khawarij, explaining their errors. Understand why their views are problematic.
4
Study the indicators of major sins
The passage provides four indicators: legal punishment, threat of punishment, explicit description as fasiq, and cursing. Note that major sins are not limited to a set number.
5
Understand the special exception for takfir
The passage quotes al-Suyuti that only lying about the Prophet leads to takfir according to Ahl al-Sunnah, which guards against extremism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولما اختلف الناس في انقسام الذنوب إلى صغائر وكبائر أشار إلى ذلك مبينا مختار أهل السنة بقوله: (ثم الذنوب) من حيث هي والذنب: ما عصي الله تعالى به، أو ما يذم مرتكبه شرعا، ويرادفه: المعصية، والخطيئة، والسيئة، والجريمة، والمنهي عنه، والمذموم شرعا. وقوله: (عندنا) أهل السنة، ظرف قدم على عامله، وهو (قسمان) لإفادة الحصر؛ فيخرج به المرجئة حيث ذهبوا إلى أنها كلها صغائر، ولا تضر مرتكبها ما دام على الإسلام، والخوارج حيث ذهبوا إلى أن كل ذنب كبيرة نظرا لعظمة من عصي به، وكل كبيرة كفر، كما يخرج به من ذهب إلى أنها كلها كبائر، ولكن لا يكفر مرتكبها إلا بما هو كفر منها، وأبدل من «قسمان» للتَّفْصيل (صَغِيرَةٌ) و(كَبيرَةٌ) فحذف العاطف، وليست الكبيرة منحصرة في عدد مذكور، وهي كما قال ابن الصلاح: كل ذنب كبر وعظم عظما يصح معه أن يطلق عليه اسم الكبير، أو وصف بكونه عظيما على الإطلاق، ولها أمارات منها: إيجاب الحد، ومنها: الإيعاد عليها بالعذاب بالنار ونحوها كان ذلك في الكتاب أو السنة، ومنها: وصف فاعلها بالفسق نصا، ومنها: اللعن، كلعن الله السارق، وأكبرها: الكفر بالله، ثم القتل العمد. قلت: في كلام الحافظ السيوطي رحمه الله تعالى ما نصه: لا أعلم شيئا من الكبائر قال أحد من أهل السنة بتكفير مرتكبه إلا الكذب على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، فإن الشيخ أبا محمد الجويني من أصحابنا وهو والد إمام الحرمين قال: إن من
When people differed regarding the division of sins into minor and major, he pointed to that, explaining the chosen view of Ahl al-Sunnah, by his saying: 'Then sins' — from the perspective of what they are, and sin (dhanb) is that by which Allah Almighty is disobeyed, or that for which its committer is legally blameworthy, and synonyms include: disobedience (ma'siyah), transgression (khati'ah), evil deed (sayyi'ah), crime (jarimah), prohibited thing, and that which is legally blameworthy. And his saying: 'with us' (Ahl al-Sunnah) is an adverbial phrase placed before its operative, and it is 'two divisions' (qismān) to indicate restriction; thereby al-Murji'ah are excluded, for they held that all sins are minor and do not harm their committer as long as he remains upon Islam, and al-Khawarij are excluded, for they held that every sin is major (kabirah) in view of the greatness of the One disobeyed, and every major sin is disbelief, and also excluded is the one who held that all sins are major, but their committer does not become a disbeliever except by that which is disbelief among them. And 'two divisions' was replaced for detail: 'minor' (saghirah) and 'major' (kabirah), omitting the conjunction. And the major sin is not restricted to a specific number, and it is, as Ibn al-Salah said: every sin that is great and immense in a way that makes it proper to call it 'major', or is described as being absolutely great. And it has indicators: among them, the imposition of the legal punishment (hadd); among them, the threat of punishment in the fire and the like, whether in the Book or the Sunnah; among them, describing its doer as a transgressor (fasiq) explicitly; among them, cursing, such as Allah's cursing of the thief. And the greatest of them is disbelief in Allah, then premeditated murder. I said: In the words of al-Hafiz al-Suyuti, may Allah have mercy on him, is the following: I know of no major sin regarding which any Ahl al-Sunnah has declared its committer a disbeliever, except lying upon the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, for Shaykh Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni, one of our companions and the father of the Imam of the Two Sanctuaries, said: Whoever...
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the Sunni position on the division of sins into major and minor. It begins by contextualizing the discussion: people differed on whether sins are divided into minor and major. The commentator then explains that the author (the poet) indicated the chosen view of Ahl al-Sunnah in his line. The term 'sin' (dhanb) is defined as that by which Allah is disobeyed, or that for which the committer is legally blameworthy, with synonyms listed. The phrase 'with us' (indana) refers to Ahl al-Sunnah, and 'two divisions' (qismān) is used for restriction (hasr), thereby excluding the Murji'ah who held all sins are minor and do not harm as long as one is Muslim, and the Khawarij who held every sin is major and constitutes disbelief, as well as those who held all sins are major but do not entail disbelief except those that are explicitly disbelief. Then the poet replaced 'two divisions' with 'minor' and 'major' for detail, omitting the conjunction. The commentator then explains that major sins are not limited to a specific number, and quotes Ibn al-Salah's definition: a sin that is great and immense to the extent that it can be called 'major', or is described as absolutely great. He then lists indicators of major sins: imposition of a legal hadd punishment, threat of punishment in the Hereafter, explicit description of the doer as fasiq (transgressor), and cursing such as Allah cursing the thief. The greatest major sin is disbelief, then premeditated murder. Finally, the commentator quotes al-Hafiz al-Suyuti, who states that no major sin, according to Ahl al-Sunnah, entails takfir (declaring the doer a disbeliever) except lying upon the Prophet, as stated by Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni. This guards against the extreme positions of the Khawarij and the Murji'ah.

Correction: The Sunni view distinguishes between major and minor sins, and only specific major sins (like lying about the Prophet) lead to disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Definition of Major Sins
Ibn al-Salah defines major sins and notes their non-fixed count.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical scholars define a major sin and why major sins are not restricted to a fixed number.

Core Idea
A major sin is any sin so great that it deserves the name 'major'.

In this lesson, we explore the foundational definition of major sins as articulated by Ibn al-Salah. The passage clarifies that major sins are not limited to a specific list, but rather identified by their severity. Understanding this definition is crucial for distinguishing between small and large sins in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the overall meaning. Then read the translation to understand the exact wording.
Notice the abrupt start with 'The section on transmitted matters' – it sets the context.
2
Identify the definition
Focus on the definition attributed to Ibn al-Salah. Note that a major sin is defined by its magnitude, not by a fixed list.
The phrase 'كُلُّ ذنبٍ كَبُرَ وعَظُمَ' is key.
3
Understand the unlimited nature
The passage explicitly states that major sins are not limited to a specific number. This corrects the misconception that only certain sins are major.
This is a direct refutation of those who claim a fixed count.
4
Reflect on implications
Think about why this matters: it allows for flexibility and prevents arbitrary restrictions on what constitutes a major sin.
This definition leaves room for scholarly discretion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم السمعيات
لتَّفصيل (صَغِيرَةٌ) و(كَبيرَةٌ) فحذف العاطف، وليست الكبيرة منحصرة في عدد مذكور ، وهي كما قال ابن الصَّلاح (۱): كُلُّ ذنبٍ كَبُرَ وعَظُمَ عِظما يصح معه أن يُطلق عليه اسم الكبير ، أو وُصِفَ بكونه عظيما على الإطلاق، ولها أمارات منها : إيجابُ الحدّ ، ومنها : الإيعَادُ عليها بالعذاب بالنار ونحوها كانَ ذلك في الكتاب أو السُّنَّة ، ومنها : وصف فاعلها بالفسق نصّا، ومنها: اللعن، كلعن الله السَّارِقَ ، وأكبرها : الكفر بالله ، ثمَّ القتل العمد (۲)(۳).
The section on transmitted matters (sam'iyyat). For detail: (small) and (large), so the conjunction is omitted. The major (sin) is not limited to a specific number. It is as Ibn al-Salah said: Every sin that becomes great and enormous in a way that the name 'major' can be applied to it, or it is described as being absolutely great. It has signs: among them is that it necessitates a prescribed punishment (hadd), and among them is the threat of punishment by fire or similar in the Book or the Sunnah, and among them is the description of its doer as sinful (fasiq) explicitly, and among them is cursing, such as Allah cursing the thief. The greatest of them is disbelief in Allah, then intentional murder.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies major sins (kaba'ir). It begins by stating that the division of sins into small and large is detailed, and that major sins are not restricted to a fixed number. Then it quotes Ibn al-Salah's definition: a major sin is one that is so great that the term 'major' applies, or it is described as absolutely great. Then it lists several signs by which a major sin can be identified: 1) it requires a prescribed legal punishment (hadd), 2) it is threatened with punishment by fire in the Quran or Sunnah, 3) its doer is explicitly called a sinner (fasiq) in the texts, and 4) it involves a curse, such as Allah cursing the thief. Finally, it states that the greatest major sin is disbelief (kufr), followed by intentional murder. This establishes a hierarchy of sins and provides criteria for identifying major sins.

Key Terms
كبائر
صغائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Major sins are limited to a specific number (e.g., seven or seventy).
Correction: The passage explicitly states major sins are not limited to a number; they are defined by their magnitude.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn al-Salah, how are major sins defined?
A) They are limited to a specific number like seven.
B) They are defined by their magnitude, not by a fixed list.
C) They are only those sins that involve cursing.
D) They are only sins that require a prescribed punishment.

Key Takeaway
A major sin is any sin whose magnitude warrants the description 'major', and it is not limited to a fixed number.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin that you consider 'small', do you treat it lightly, forgetting that any sin could become 'major' if it meets the criterion of greatness? How does this definition challenge your daily attitude towards minor sins?
?
You know that major sins are not a fixed list. So what if you commit a sin that you haven't classified as major? Does your conscience still feel the weight of it? What does that tell you about your awareness of Allah's view of your actions?
?
If a sin can be considered major because it is 'described as being absolutely great', can you think of a sin you rationalize that Allah describes in the Quran as 'great'? Will you repent from it today?

Signs of Major Sins
Ibn al-Salah lists four signs of major sins and their relative severity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four signs of major sins and know the greatest major sins according to Ibn al-Salah.

Core Idea
Major sins are known by signs: prescribed punishment, threat of fire, being called fasiq, or being cursed.

Having established the definition, Ibn al-Salah provides practical signs to identify major sins. These signs are derived from the Quran and Sunnah. This lesson will cover each sign and also reveal the greatest major sins: disbelief and murder.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on signs
Read the Arabic passage focusing on the signs of major sins. The translation will help clarify the terms.
Notice the structure: 'منها' introduces each sign.
2
Identify the four signs

These signs are not exhaustive but indicative.
3
Understand the hierarchy
The passage ends by stating the greatest major sins: disbelief (kufr) followed by intentional murder.
This shows that not all major sins are equal in gravity.
4
Reflect on practical application
How can these signs help a Muslim identify major sins in daily life? Think about sins that fit these criteria.
This classification aids in repentance and piety.

لتَّفصيل (صَغِيرَةٌ) و(كَبيرَةٌ) فحذف العاطف، وليست الكبيرة منحصرة في عدد مذكور ، وهي كما قال ابن الصَّلاح (۱): كُلُّ ذنبٍ كَبُرَ وعَظُمَ عِظما يصح معه أن يُطلق عليه اسم الكبير ، أو وُصِفَ بكونه عظيما على الإطلاق، ولها أمارات منها : إيجابُ الحدّ ، ومنها : الإيعَادُ عليها بالعذاب بالنار ونحوها كانَ ذلك في الكتاب أو السُّنَّة ، ومنها : وصف فاعلها بالفسق نصّا، ومنها: اللعن، كلعن الله السَّارِقَ ، وأكبرها : الكفر بالله ، ثمَّ القتل العمد (۲)(۳).
The section on transmitted matters (sam'iyyat). For detail: (small) and (large), so the conjunction is omitted. The major (sin) is not limited to a specific number. It is as Ibn al-Salah said: Every sin that becomes great and enormous in a way that the name 'major' can be applied to it, or it is described as being absolutely great. It has signs: among them is that it necessitates a prescribed punishment (hadd), and among them is the threat of punishment by fire or similar in the Book or the Sunnah, and among them is the description of its doer as sinful (fasiq) explicitly, and among them is cursing, such as Allah cursing the thief. The greatest of them is disbelief in Allah, then intentional murder.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies major sins (kaba'ir). It begins by stating that the division of sins into small and large is detailed, and that major sins are not restricted to a fixed number. Then it quotes Ibn al-Salah's definition: a major sin is one that is so great that the term 'major' applies, or it is described as absolutely great. Then it lists several signs by which a major sin can be identified: 1) it requires a prescribed legal punishment (hadd), 2) it is threatened with punishment by fire in the Quran or Sunnah, 3) its doer is explicitly called a sinner (fasiq) in the texts, and 4) it involves a curse, such as Allah cursing the thief. Finally, it states that the greatest major sin is disbelief (kufr), followed by intentional murder. This establishes a hierarchy of sins and provides criteria for identifying major sins.

Key Terms
إيجاب الحد
الإيعاد
الفسق
اللعن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All sins are equally grave and there is no distinction between major and minor.
Correction: This passage shows that major sins have specific signs and that even among major sins there is a hierarchy, with disbelief and murder being the worst.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the signs of a major sin mentioned in the passage?
A) It necessitates a prescribed punishment (hadd).
B) The doer is described as fasiq.
C) It is committed by a non-Muslim.
D) Allah curses the doer.

Key Takeaway
Major sins have four identifiable signs, and the greatest of them are disbelief and intentional murder.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the four signs does your own conscience recognize in a sin you struggle with? How will you respond today to that warning before it is too late?
?
If the greatest sin is disbelief, what is the state of your own iman? Are you taking steps to protect it from the smaller sins that may lead to kufr?
?
The source says Allah curses the thief. Do you ever excuse minor theft or dishonesty? How can you root out that subtle disregard for the law of Allah?

Unseen Matters
intermediate
4 min
Lying About the Prophet: The Greatest Sin
Author rules deliberate lying about the Prophet as kufr and greatest sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why deliberate lying about the Prophet is considered the greatest major sin and how it differs from other sins.

Core Idea
Lying about the Prophet is uniquely kufr, making it the greatest sin.

This lesson examines a powerful ruling that distinguishes one sin above all others. The author divides sins into major and minor, then singles out deliberate lying about the Prophet as an act of disbelief. Through this, we see the unique severity of this sin and why it is considered the greatest major sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's ruling stand out.
Notice the two parts: general division and specific ruling.
2
Identify the two components
Look for the general division of sins into major and minor, and then the specific ruling on lying about the Prophet.
The ruling explicitly says it causes kufr that takes one out of the religion.
3
Understand the argument
See how the author concludes that this sin is the greatest major sin because no other major sin entails kufr according to Ahl al-Sunnah.
The logic: unique severity → greatest sin.
4
Reflect on scholarly support
Note that a group of scholars, including Imam Ibn al-Munir, supported this view. This adds weight to the ruling.
5
Contrast with other sins
Understand that other major sins, however grave, do not remove one from the religion. This highlights the exceptional nature of lying about the Prophet.
This contrast is key to understanding the hierarchy of sins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انقسام الذنوب إلى كبائر وصغائر. تعمد الكذب عليه صلى الله عليه وسلم يكفر كفرا يخرجه عن الملة، وتبعه على ذلك طائفة منهم الإمام ناصر الدين ابن المنير من أئمة المالكية، وهذا يدل على أنه أكبر الكبائر، لأنه لا شيء من الكبائر يقتضي الكفر عند أحد من أهل السنة، انتهى
The division of sins into major and minor. Deliberate lying about him (peace be upon him) causes disbelief (kufr) that takes one out of the religion, and a group followed him in that, among them Imam Nasir al-Din Ibn al-Munir from the Malikite imams. And this indicates that it is the greatest of major sins, because no major sin entails disbelief according to any of the Ahl al-Sunnah. End.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal ruling that classifies sins and singles out a specific sin. It begins by stating the general division of sins into major and minor. Then it gives a specific ruling: deliberately lying about the Prophet is disbelief that removes one from Islam. It notes that a group of scholars, including the Maliki scholar Ibn al-Munir, supported this view. The author argues that this proves lying about the Prophet is the greatest major sin, because no other major sin is considered disbelief by the Ahl al-Sunnah. Thus the conclusion follows from the premise that only this sin entails kufr.

Key Terms
كبائر
صغائر
كفر
تعمد الكذب
أكبر الكبائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All major sins are equal in gravity; none removes one from Islam.
Correction: Lying about the Prophet is uniquely kufr, making it the greatest major sin, unlike any other sin.

Checkpoint
What does the author say about deliberate lying about the Prophet?
A) It is a major sin like any other major sin.
B) It is kufr that takes one out of the religion.
C) It is a minor sin.
D) It is only forbidden but not kufr.

Key Takeaway
Deliberate lying about the Prophet is kufr and thus the greatest major sin, unlike any other sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear or share a hadith without checking its authenticity, do you realize you are risking falling into the sin of lying about the Prophet? What will you change today in your approach to transmitting religious knowledge?
?
If you truly believed that lying about the Prophet is kufr that takes you out of Islam, would you be as careless as you sometimes are about verifying what you attribute to him? What specific habit will you break to ensure you never commit this sin?
?
Reflect: you may consider yourself a Muslim, but have you ever treated the Prophet's words lightly—misquoting, exaggerating, or fabricating a teaching for your own benefit? How does this lesson expose the state of your heart, and what will you do to repent sincerely?
